Defending Talha and Zubayr: The Meaning of 'Baghi'
Nasafi refutes the charge that Talha and Zubayr were sinners or oppressors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Nasafi argues that Talha and Zubayr should not be called oppressors or sinners, and how the term 'baghi' can mean 'seeker' without moral condemnation.

Core Idea
Being a 'baghi' doesn't always mean being a sinner — context matters.

This passage addresses a sensitive historical issue: the labeling of Talha and Zubayr, two prominent Companions, as rebels. Nasafi uses a legal analogy and a reinterpretation of a hadith to defend them. He argues that their actions were motivated by justice, not worldly ambition, and that calling them oppressors is unjustified.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the key legal ruling
Find the inheritance ruling from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Notice how it equates the baghi with the just person in this context, implying the baghi is not inherently sinful.
3
Understand the hadith reinterpretation
See how those who refuse to label Talha and Zubayr as baghi reinterpret the hadith about Ammar, explaining 'baghi' as 'seeker' rather than 'rebel'.
4
Recognize the refutation of Rawafid labels
Note how Nasafi dismisses the labels 'oppressor' and 'sinner' used by the Rawafid, based on the Companions' true intentions.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that calling Talha and Zubayr oppressors is not permissible given their actions and motives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تسميتهم فساقًا لما مر، ولهذا ألحق أصحابنا رحمهم الله تأويلهم الفاسد بالصحيح في حق إبطال المؤاخذة، ولهذا قال أبو حنيفة ومحمد – رحمهم الله -: إن الباغي إذا قتل مورثه العادل لا يحرم من الميراث كما لو قتل العادل مورثه. ومن امتنع عن إطلاق اسم الباغي على هؤلاء يؤول قوله عليه السلام الباغي لعمار: 'تقتلك الفئة الباغية' فيقول: معناه الطائفة الطالبة دم عثمان، يقال: بغى إذا طلب. ولا يلتفت إلى إطلاق الروافض اسم الظالم والفاسق وغير ذلك، لما أقمنا من الدلالة على انتفاء هذه السمات عنهم. وكيف يجوز إطلاق هذه الأسامي على من كان ساعيًا في تحقيق الحق وإبطال الباطل وطالبًا لما هو الواجب في ظاهر الشريعة من إيجاب القصاص غير ساع في الاستيلاء على الملك والترأس على الخلائق لينازع غيره ويزيل سلطانه إلى نفسه؟ ولهذا امتنع طلحة والزبير عن تقلد الإمامة والدخول في الخلافة بعد مقتل عثمان – الله يأبى ذلك أشد الإباء – إلى أن تبين له بمشورة أجلاء الصحابة وجه المصلحة في ذلك على ما مر ذكره. وإذا كان الأمر كذلك لم تكن تسميتهم بالظالم والفاسق جائزة مع ما بينا من ذلك، والله الموفق.
Their calling them sinners because of what has passed, and therefore our companions – may Allah have mercy on them – attached their corrupt interpretation to the correct one in the matter of nullifying accountability, and therefore Abu Hanifa and Muhammad – may Allah have mercy on them – said: Indeed, the rebel (al-bāghī) when he kills his just inheritor is not deprived of inheritance just as when the just person kills his inheritor. And whoever refrains from applying the name rebel to these [people] interprets the Prophet’s saying – peace be upon him – about Ammar: 'The rebellious group (al-fi'a al-bāghiya) will kill you.' He says: Its meaning is the group seeking the blood of Uthman; it is said: baghā when he seeks. And no attention is paid to the Rawafid's application of the name oppressor (al-ẓālim) and sinner (al-fāsiq) and other than that, because we have established proof of the negation of these characteristics from them. And how is it permissible to apply these names to one who was striving to establish truth and abolish falsehood and seeking what is obligatory according to the apparent Sharia of establishing retribution, not striving to seize dominion and take headship over creation to contend with others and remove his authority to himself? And for this, Talha and al-Zubayr refrained from assuming the imamate and entering the caliphate after the killing of Uthman – Allah forbids that strongly – until the aspect of benefit became clear to them through the consultation of the senior companions, as has been mentioned before. And when the matter is like this, calling them oppressors and sinners is not permissible, along with what we have clarified of that. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 520

Commentary
This passage defends Talha, Zubayr, and those involved in the Battle of the Camel against being labeled as sinners or oppressors. It begins by referencing an earlier point about calling them sinners, then connects it to a ruling by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: when a rebel (baghi) kills a just person, the rebel does not lose inheritance rights, just as a just person does not lose inheritance if he kills his inheritor. This ruling implies that the term 'baghi' does not inherently carry sinfulness in this context, as the rebels here were seeking justice for Uthman. The passage then addresses those who object to applying the term 'baghi' to these Companions by reinterpreting the hadith about Ammar ('The rebellious group will kill you') as meaning 'the group seeking the blood of Uthman,' noting that the Arabic root 'baghi' means 'to seek.' It dismisses the labels 'oppressor' and 'sinner' used by the Rawafid, because the Companions in question were actually striving to establish truth and enforce retribution (qisas) for Uthman's killing, not seeking worldly power. Evidence is given: Talha and Zubayr refrained from claiming the caliphate until after consulting senior companions and recognizing the public interest. The conclusion is firm: applying 'oppressor' or 'sinner' to them is not permissible.

Key Terms
باغٍ
فئة باغية
ظالم
فاسق
روافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Calling someone a 'baghi' automatically implies they are sinful and deserve condemnation.
Correction: The inheritance ruling shows that a baghi's sinfulness is not absolute, and the hadith reinterpretation shows 'baghi' can simply mean 'seeker' without moral judgment.

Checkpoint
How do Abu Hanifa and Muhammad prove that the label 'baghi' does not necessarily entail sin in this context?
A) By citing a hadith that the baghi is always forgiven.
B) By ruling that a baghi who kills his just inheritor does not lose inheritance, just like a just person.
C) By stating that Talha and Zubayr were not actually rebels.
D) By rejecting the hadith about Ammar.

Key Takeaway
The term 'baghi' in the context of the Companions does not necessarily imply sin; their motivation was justice, not rebellion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone criticize a Companion like Talha or Zubayr, do you immediately accept the criticism or do you pause to investigate their motives? Nasafi's careful analysis shows that labels can be misleading. What will you do next time you encounter such criticism to ensure you are not unfairly judging those whom Allah has praised?
?
The passage presents Talha and Zubayr as seekers of truth and justice, not power. Ask yourself: in your daily actions, are you primarily motivated by seeking Allah's approval and justice, or are you driven by personal gain, recognition, or power? Identify one specific area where you need to purify your intention.
?
Nasafi dismisses the labels of the Rawafid because they contradict established proofs. Are there people or groups you have judged based on labels without examining the full context and evidence? Commit to learning the full story before forming an opinion about anyone, especially figures from Islamic history.

6 min
The Ideal of Refraining and the Necessity of Recording
Author states the ideal and then the necessity for recording.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the scholars of Ahl al-Sunna recorded the disputes among the Companions despite the command to refrain, and how this action safeguards faith.

Core Idea
Recording Companions' disputes protects hearts from false beliefs.

The author begins by affirming that the safest course is to refrain from discussing the Companions' conflicts. However, he explains that a greater necessity arose: to prevent the spread of incorrect beliefs about them. This lesson explores the reasoning behind the scholarly decision to document these events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the ideal of refraining
Read the passage once without analysis. Note how the author states that silence is safer and more in line with the Prophet's command.
2
Understand the necessity that overrode the ideal
Notice the shift: the author argues that hearts cannot be forced to refrain even if tongues are silent, so mentioning became necessary to prevent harmful speculation.
This is the key turning point in the argument.
3
Recognize the role of preservers and theologians
The author explains that the huffāẓ and mutakallimūn undertook the recording and explanation to protect correct belief about the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وترك اغتنام أموالهم، وغير ذلك من الأحكام التي أخذها فقهاء الأمة عن معاملة عليه وسيرته فيهم حتى قال أبو حنيفة – قدس الله روحه -: "لولا علي لم نكن نعرف السيرة في الخوارج لكان الكف عن ذكر أحوالهم والإغضاء عما جرى بينهم ودفع أحوالهم جملةً عن القلوب والألسن أسلم في الدين وأوفق بما مَنَّ الله علينا في تأخير انتسابنا عن الوقف الذي فيه خوف الاشتراك فيما لا يحل في الدين، والميل إلى ما الحق في غيره، وأقرب إلى ما دل عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: "إذا ذكر أصحابي فأمسكوا وفي الخوض في أحوالهم مع إمساك اللسان انتشار القلوب لأن القلوب لا تمتنع عن فعلها وذلك أشد من الألسن، إلا أن الحالة التي بيناها دعتنا إلى ذكر أحوالهم والإخبار عما جرى بينهم، فقام حفاظ الأمة بذكرها والمتكلمون بالكشف عن وجوه ذلك، صيانةً للقلوب عن اعتقاد ما لا يحل فيهم مع ما أكرمهم الله تعالى به من صحبة النبي، ونصرة دينه، ونقل شريعته، وتبليغ وحيه، ثم إن فقهاء الأمة أخذوا ذلك عن معاملة علي، ثم يجوز أن يكون ذلك قد عرف النبي عليه السلام غيره لكنهم لم يخرجوا إلى وقت علي، ورأوا بالذي فعله هو الله كفاية إذ لم يغيروا عليه، وكان فعله ظاهراً بحيث عرفه الكل، وبلغ مبلغا لو ظهر منه منكر ليلزم التغيير، ويجوز أن يكون خصه النبي عليه السلام بتعليم الأحكام بما قد علم أنه يخص بالحاجة إلى ذلك، وفي قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إنا نقاتل على التنزيل وأنت تقاتل على التأويل" دليل أن جميع ما فعل فعل عن علم وعلى موافقة الشريعة، والله أعلم.
ثم في جميع ما جرى من علي وأتباعه من المعاملة مع مخالفيهم والامتناع عن أن يعاملوهم معاملة الكفار أو المرتدين بل قال: إخواننا بغوا علينا – وقوله لابن طلحة: أنا وأبوك من أهل هذه الآية (وَنَزَعْنَا مَا فِي صُدُورِهِم مِّنْ عَل) دلالة بغض قول المعتزلة والخوارج، والله الموفق.
And refraining from taking their property, and other rulings that the jurists of the community took from the dealing of Ali and his conduct with them, until Abu Hanifa – may Allah sanctify his soul – said: 'Were it not for Ali, we would not know the sīra regarding the Khawarij. Indeed, refraining from mentioning their states, and overlooking what occurred between them, and removing their states altogether from hearts and tongues would be safer in religion and more suitable to what Allah has favored us with in delaying our affiliation from the stop that entails fear of sharing in what is not permissible in religion, and inclining to what is right in other than it, and closer to what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) indicated by his saying: "If my companions are mentioned, then refrain." And delving into their states while restraining the tongue causes the hearts to spread, because hearts do not refrain from their action, and that is more severe than tongues. Except that the situation we described called us to mention their states and inform of what occurred between them. So the preservers of the community undertook their mention, and the theologians (mutakallimūn) undertook the disclosure of the aspects of that, as a protection of hearts from believing what is not permissible regarding them, despite what Allah the Exalted honored them with of the companionship of the Prophet, and supporting His religion, and transmitting His law, and conveying His revelation. Then the jurists of the community took that from the dealing of Ali. Then it is possible that the Prophet (peace be upon him) had taught others besides him, but they did not emerge until the time of Ali. And they saw that what he did was sufficient from Allah, since they did not change it. And his action was apparent such that everyone knew it, and it reached a level such that if any wrong had appeared from him, change would have been necessary. And it is possible that the Prophet (peace be upon him) specially taught him the rulings, knowing that he would be specially needed for that. And in his saying (peace be upon him): "We fight over the revelation and you fight over the interpretation" is evidence that all that he did was done with knowledge and in accordance with the Sharia. And Allah knows best. Then in all that occurred from Ali and his followers of dealing with their opponents, and refraining from treating them as disbelievers or apostates, rather he said: 'Our brothers have wronged us' – and his saying to Ibn Talha: 'I and your father are among the people of this verse: "And We shall remove from their breasts any rancor"' – is an indication of the falsehood of the saying of the Mu'tazila and the Khawarij. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 521

Commentary
This passage is a justification for why the scholars recorded the events that occurred between the Companions, despite the general command to refrain from discussing their disputes. The author begins by stating the ideal: refraining from mentioning their states and overlooking what happened would be safer in religion. He quotes Abu Hanifa, who emphasizes the indispensability of Ali's example in knowing the proper treatment of the Khawarij. However, the author then explains that the actual situation necessitated recording these events to protect hearts from false beliefs about the Companions. Thus, the preservers (huffāẓ) of the community undertook to transmit these accounts, and the theologians (mutakallimūn) clarified their aspects to safeguard correct belief. The author then addresses possible objections: it is possible that the Prophet taught others besides Ali, but they did not become prominent until Ali's time; Ali's actions were so public that any error would have been corrected; and the Prophet's hadith about fighting over revelation versus interpretation confirms that Ali acted with knowledge and in accordance with the Sharia. Finally, the author concludes by noting that Ali's treatment of his opponents as brothers, and his quote to Ibn Talha, refute the claims of the Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Key Terms
صحابة
خوارج
سيرة
إمساك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Recording the Companions' disputes shows that Ahl al-Sunna approves of discord among them.
Correction: The passage explicitly says recording was done to protect hearts from false beliefs, not to promote discord.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did the scholars record the disputes among the Companions despite the command to refrain from mentioning them?
A) To preserve historical accuracy for future generations.
B) To protect hearts from believing what is not permissible about the Companions.
C) To justify the actions of Ali specifically.
D) To encourage debate about theological matters.

Key Takeaway
The scholars recorded Companions' disputes not for gossip but to protect the faith from false interpretations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about disagreements among the Companions, what is your heart's immediate reaction—curiosity, judgment, or trust in their overall righteousness? This lesson warns that hearts do not refrain even if tongues are silent. Today, examine your inner thoughts about the Companions. If you find any negative assumption, repent and actively learn the correct perspective from reliable scholars.
?
The ideal was to refrain entirely, but necessity forced the scholars to record and explain. Is there a difficult issue in your own life that you avoid because it seems safer to ignore, but that avoidance is allowing your heart to drift into false assumptions? What step will you take this week to address it in a way that protects your faith rather than your comfort?
?
The scholars recorded the disputes to protect hearts from believing what is not permissible about the Companions. Have you ever formed an opinion about a Companion based on incomplete or biased sources? How will you ensure that your knowledge about the Companions comes from trustworthy sources and that your heart remains pure towards all of them?

7 min
The Evidences from Ali and the Prophet
Author provides evidence from Ali and the Prophet to justify the approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali's role and the Prophet's hadith justify the approach taken by the jurists and refute the claims of the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Ali's actions were guided by prophetic knowledge, validating the Sunni approach.

After establishing the necessity of recording, the author now provides scriptural and historical evidence. He explains that the jurists based their rulings on Ali's example, possibly taught specially by the Prophet. The Prophet's hadith about fighting over interpretation further confirms Ali's correctness, and finally, Ali's own words refute the Khawarij and Mu'tazila.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the jurists' reliance on Ali
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice how the author links the jurists' rulings directly to Ali's conduct.
2
Consider the possibilities of prophetic teaching
The author presents two possibilities: the Prophet taught others who awaited Ali's time, or He specially taught Ali. Think about why this supports the authenticity of the rulings.
The public nature of Ali's actions also serves as a check.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Focus on the hadith: 'We fight over the revelation, you fight over the interpretation.' What does it prove about Ali's actions?
4
Understand the refutation of Khawarij and Mu'tazila
Read how Ali called his opponents brothers and quoted the verse about removing rancor. This directly refutes the positions of the Khawarij (who declared them disbelievers) and the Mu'tazila (who condemned them as sinners).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وترك اغتنام أموالهم، وغير ذلك من الأحكام التي أخذها فقهاء الأمة عن معاملة عليه وسيرته فيهم حتى قال أبو حنيفة – قدس الله روحه -: "لولا علي لم نكن نعرف السيرة في الخوارج لكان الكف عن ذكر أحوالهم والإغضاء عما جرى بينهم ودفع أحوالهم جملةً عن القلوب والألسن أسلم في الدين وأوفق بما مَنَّ الله علينا في تأخير انتسابنا عن الوقف الذي فيه خوف الاشتراك فيما لا يحل في الدين، والميل إلى ما الحق في غيره، وأقرب إلى ما دل عليه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بقوله: "إذا ذكر أصحابي فأمسكوا وفي الخوض في أحوالهم مع إمساك اللسان انتشار القلوب لأن القلوب لا تمتنع عن فعلها وذلك أشد من الألسن، إلا أن الحالة التي بيناها دعتنا إلى ذكر أحوالهم والإخبار عما جرى بينهم، فقام حفاظ الأمة بذكرها والمتكلمون بالكشف عن وجوه ذلك، صيانةً للقلوب عن اعتقاد ما لا يحل فيهم مع ما أكرمهم الله تعالى به من صحبة النبي، ونصرة دينه، ونقل شريعته، وتبليغ وحيه، ثم إن فقهاء الأمة أخذوا ذلك عن معاملة علي، ثم يجوز أن يكون ذلك قد عرف النبي عليه السلام غيره لكنهم لم يخرجوا إلى وقت علي، ورأوا بالذي فعله هو الله كفاية إذ لم يغيروا عليه، وكان فعله ظاهراً بحيث عرفه الكل، وبلغ مبلغا لو ظهر منه منكر ليلزم التغيير، ويجوز أن يكون خصه النبي عليه السلام بتعليم الأحكام بما قد علم أنه يخص بالحاجة إلى ذلك، وفي قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "إنا نقاتل على التنزيل وأنت تقاتل على التأويل" دليل أن جميع ما فعل فعل عن علم وعلى موافقة الشريعة، والله أعلم.
ثم في جميع ما جرى من علي وأتباعه من المعاملة مع مخالفيهم والامتناع عن أن يعاملوهم معاملة الكفار أو المرتدين بل قال: إخواننا بغوا علينا – وقوله لابن طلحة: أنا وأبوك من أهل هذه الآية (وَنَزَعْنَا مَا فِي صُدُورِهِم مِّنْ عَل) دلالة بغض قول المعتزلة والخوارج، والله الموفق.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's treatment of the Khawarij was a personal ijtihad not supported by the Prophet.
Correction: The author provides evidence that the Prophet supported Ali's actions, and they were in accordance with Sharia.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Prophet's statement 'We fight over the revelation, you fight over the interpretation' indicate?
A) Ali was permitted to make his own rulings independently.
B) Ali's actions were in accordance with the Sharia.
C) Ali was superior to other Companions.
D) The revelation was incomplete.

Key Takeaway
Ali's treatment of his opponents as brothers and the Prophet's support validate the Sunni approach.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim commit a sin or hold a different view, do you instinctively distance yourself or treat them as a brother? How would Ali's example change your response?
?
Are you quick to label others as outside the fold of Islam based on your own understanding? What would it take for you to instead say 'our brothers have rebelled against us'?
?
Which of the two justifications in the passage (Prophet taught others but they waited, or Prophet specifically instructed Ali) do you find more convincing? How does your preference reveal your own assumptions about prophetic guidance?

The Wisdom of Imamate: Defending Ali's Arbitration
Author defends Ali's arbitration decision against Kharijite criticism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Sunni scholars defended Ali's decision to accept arbitration and how the higher purpose of imamate (unifying hearts) guided that decision.

Core Idea
True leadership seeks unity, not conflict — even against rebels.

The Khawarij accused Ali of abandoning the obligation to fight rebels by accepting arbitration. Sunni scholars responded by pointing to a deeper principle: the purpose of imamate is to bring hearts together, and war is only permitted when other means fail. This passage lays out that argument clearly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two positions
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Note the Sunni position and the Kharijite objection.
The Kharijite objection is based on a Quranic verse about fighting rebels.
2
Understand the Kharijite proof and the Sunni counter-argument
The Khawarij cite the verse to argue Ali should have fought. The author refutes by explaining the wisdom of imamate: unifying hearts.
3
Reflect on the delayed obligation of jihad
The author argues that jihad was delayed until other means fail. Consider how this supports the priority of unity over conflict.
This shows that fighting is not the first option in Islamic governance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الكلام في التحكيم فذهب أصحابنا وجميع أهل السنة إلى أن عليا كان مصيبًا في التحكيم، وزعمت الخوارج أنه كان مخطئًا فيه وقد كفر، إذ كان الواجب من أهل البغي هو المحاربة على ما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَإِنْ بَغَتْ إِحْدَتهُمَا عَلَى الْأُخْرَىٰ فَقَتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي حَتَّى تَفِيءَ إِلَى أَمْرِ الله ﴾ الآية، ولكن أصحابنا – رحمهم الله – قالوا: إن هذا قول من جهل حكمة الإمامة وعظم منزلتهما في أمر الدين والسياسة، فإن حكمة الإمامة إنما جلت ومنزلتها عظمت بما فيها من تألف الخلق واجتماع القلوب اللذين هما سبب الأمن والبقاء، وبهما الوفاء في كل مرتضى من الأفعال والأقوال، والبلوغ إلى كل مرتقى من الفضائل والآداب، وجعلت الحروب للتألف بُعد عن إصابته بسائر أسباب التألف من المحاجات وأنواع البر. ولذلك – والله أعلم – أخر الله فرض الجهاد والقتال عن سائر أنواع الفرائض حتى ينتهي أسباب التأليف والتفريق لها ثم تظهر المكابرات للعقول، والمعاندات للحق، وتزول منفعة المحاجة وأنواع البر واللطف فوضع القتال ليكون التألف بذلك، ولذلك عظم الله مننه على الخلق بتأليف القلوب فقال : ( وَأَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ لَوْ أَنفَقْتَ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا مَّا
As for the discussion on arbitration, our companions and all the People of the Sunnah hold that Ali was correct in the arbitration, while the Khawarij claim that he was mistaken in it and became an unbeliever, since the obligation regarding the rebellious party is to fight them, as Allah the Exalted said: 'But if one of them transgresses against the other, then fight the one that transgresses until it returns to the command of Allah' – the verse. But our companions – may Allah have mercy on them – said: This is the saying of one who is ignorant of the wisdom of the imamate and the greatness of their status in the matter of religion and politics. For the wisdom of the imamate is great and its status is exalted only by what it contains of bringing people together and uniting hearts, which are the cause of security and survival, and by them is fulfillment in every approved action and speech, and attainment of every high rank of virtues and manners. And wars are set for unification, not for destruction, using other means of unification such as debates and types of goodness. For this reason – and Allah knows best – Allah delayed the obligation of jihad and fighting from other types of obligations until the causes of unification and division for it are exhausted, then obstinacy appears to minds, and opposition to truth, and the benefit of debate and types of goodness and kindness ceases, so He placed fighting so that unification is achieved by that. For this reason Allah magnified His favor upon the creation by uniting hearts, saying: 'And He united their hearts; if you had spent all that is in the earth, you could not have united their hearts, but Allah united them.'
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Ali's decision to accept arbitration (taḥkīm) against the Khawarij. The author first states the Sunni consensus: Ali was correct. He then presents the Kharijite objection based on the Quranic verse commanding to fight the rebellious party until they return to Allah's command – implying that Ali should have continued fighting rather than arbitrating. The author refutes this by explaining that the Khawarij's view stems from ignorance of the higher wisdom of imamate. The true purpose of imamate is to unify hearts and bring people together, which is the foundation of security and survival. War is not an end in itself; it is only used as a last resort when other means of unification (such as debate and acts of goodness) fail. The author supports this by noting that Allah delayed the obligation of jihad until after other means are exhausted. Finally, he cites the Quranic verse about Allah uniting hearts to emphasize that unification is a divine favor greater than any material expenditure. The incomplete verse underscores that unity comes from Allah.

Key Terms
تحكيم
خوارج
إمامة
تألف
بغي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Fighting rebels is always obligatory without considering the higher objectives of Sharia.
Correction: The passage shows that the priority is unifying hearts; war is only when other means fail.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary wisdom of the imamate that the Khawarij ignored?
A) Enforcing strict punishment on rebels.
B) Unifying hearts and bringing people together.
C) Maintaining a standing army for jihad.
D) Establishing a single caliphate.

Key Takeaway
The primary purpose of leadership in Islam is to unify hearts; even in rebellion, the goal is reconciliation, not punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone offends or wrongs you, what is your first impulse: to fight back or to seek understanding? How does Ali's example of prioritizing unity challenge you to change that impulse? What concrete step will you take the next time you feel wronged?
?
The Kharijites clung to a literal command while missing the greater wisdom behind it. In your own practice of Islam, are there areas where you focus on the letter of the law but neglect the spirit? Identify one such area and commit to rethinking your approach this week.
?
The passage says the imamate's greatness lies in uniting hearts. Are you a unifier or a divider in your family, workplace, or social circle? Name one specific relationship where you can actively work to bring hearts together, and write down when you will do it.

Ali's Treatment of Opponents: Evidence from His Conduct
Author cites Ali's conduct as evidence against Mu'tazila and Khawarij.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ali's treatment of his opponents provides evidence against the Mu'tazila and Khawarij positions on excommunication.

Core Idea
Ali called his opponents 'brothers'—a proof they were not disbelievers.

This short passage from Tabṣirat al-Adilla presents a key piece of evidence from the conduct of Ali ibn Abī Ṭālib and his followers. The author argues that Ali did not treat his opponents as disbelievers or apostates, but rather as brothers who had wronged him. This directly contradicts the claims of the Muʿtazila and Khawārij, who held extreme views on judging opponents. Let's examine the text and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the key phrases: 'our brothers have wronged us' and the Quranic verse about removing rancor.
The passage is concise but packed with meaning.
2
Identify Ali's actual treatment
Identify how Ali treated his opponents: he called them 'brothers' and refrained from treating them as disbelievers or apostates. He also quoted a Quranic verse that implies they are believers.
This contrasts with the harsh treatment prescribed by extremists.
3
Understand the refutation
Reflect on how this conduct serves as evidence against the Mu'tazila and Khawarij, who believed that grave sinners or political opponents become disbelievers. Ali's brotherly address shows they remained Muslims.
The author concludes that this is a clear refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم في جميع ما جرى من علي وأتباعه من المعاملة مع مخالفيهم والامتناع عن أن يعاملوهم معاملة الكفار أو المرتدين بل قال : إخواننا بغوا علينا – وقوله لابن طلحة - أنا وأبوك من أهل هذه الآية (وَنَزَعْنَا مَا فِي صُدُورِهِم مِّنْ عَل ) دلالة بغض قول المعتزلة والخوارج، والله الموفق.
Then, in all that happened from Ali and his followers in dealings with their opponents, and refraining from treating them as disbelievers or apostates—rather he said: 'Our brothers have wronged us'—and his saying to Ibn Talha: 'I and your father are among the people of this verse (And We shall remove from their breasts any rancor)' is evidence against the statement of the Mu'tazila and the Khawarij. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage presents evidence from Ali's conduct toward his opponents to refute the Mu'tazila and Khawarij. The author notes that Ali and his followers did not treat their opponents as disbelievers or apostates, but rather called them 'our brothers' and cited the Quranic verse about removing rancor from hearts. This shows that the Mu'tazila and Khawarij are wrong in their extreme positions about judging opponents. The passage ends with a prayer for divine success.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
الخوارج
علي بن أبي طالب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How did Ali address his opponents according to this passage?
A) As disbelievers
B) As apostates
C) As brothers who wronged him
D) As enemies of God

Key Takeaway
Ali's brotherly address to his opponents confirms that they remained Muslims despite their opposition, refuting extremist positions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a fellow Muslim who disagrees with you on a religious matter, do you internally categorize them as a 'brother' or as an outsider? How does Ali's example challenge your natural inclination to distance yourself from those you oppose? What concrete step can you take this week to treat such a person as a brother despite your disagreement?
?
Ali included his adversary's father in the hopeful vision of the Quranic verse about the removal of rancor. Is there someone in your life toward whom you hold a grudge? Would you be willing to pray for that person's inclusion in Paradise? What would it take for you to release that bitterness and sincerely wish for their well-being?
?
The author presents Ali's conduct as decisive evidence against those who declare others disbelievers. Are there Muslims whose faith you have doubted because of their actions? How does this lesson press you to reconsider your judgment? Will you stop questioning their Islam and instead see them as a brother or sister in need of correction, not excommunication?

The Wisdom of Arbitration and the Purpose of Imamate
Author explains the wisdom of arbitration and imamate's purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that arbitration reflects the core purpose of the imamate: uniting hearts and achieving security.

Core Idea
Arbitration is the highest wisdom of imamate for unity, not weakness.

The Khawarij claimed that Ali erred by agreeing to arbitration instead of fighting. The author counters that this objection stems from ignorance of the imamate's true purpose—to unite hearts and bring security. This passage explains how arbitration aligns with that purpose, supported by Quranic and prophetic precedents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sunni position
Read the opening where the author states that Ahl al-Sunna consider Ali correct in arbitration, while Khawarij consider him mistaken and disbelieving.
The Khawarij based their objection on the Quranic command to fight aggressors.
2
Understand the wisdom of imamate
Focus on the lines describing the purpose of imamate: uniting hearts, ensuring security, and enabling virtues. Fighting is a last resort, not the primary goal.
The author says fighting is only for when other means of unity fail.
3
See the Quranic and prophetic evidence
Notice the verses about uniting hearts and the examples of arbitration between spouses and the Prophet's treaty with Mecca. These show that arbitration is a legitimate tool for unity.
The author connects Ali's action to these precedents.
4
Appreciate Ali's motivation
The passage says Ali saw weariness in his troops and sought to achieve unity without further bloodshed. This was an act of compassion, not error.
The Arabic uses 'سآمة' (weariness) and 'رجاء' (hope).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على وقضية التحكيم] وأما الكلام في التحكيم فذهب أصحابنا وجميع أهل السنة إلى أن عليا كان مصيبًا في التحكيم، وزعمت الخوارج أنه كان مخطئًا فيه وقد كفر، إذ كان الواجب من أهل البغي هو المحاربة على ما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فَإِنْ بَغَتْ إِحْدَتهُمَا عَلَى الْأُخْرَىٰ فَقَتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي حَتَّى تَفِيءَ إِلَى أَمْرِ الله ) الآية، ولكن أصحابنا – رحمهم الله – قالوا: إن هذا قول من جهل حكمة الإمامة وعظم منزلتهما في أمر الدين والسياسة، فإن حكمة الإمامة إنما جلت ومنزلتها عظمت بما فيها من تألف الخلق واجتماع القلوب اللذين هما سبب الأمن والبقاء، وبهما الوفاء في كل مرتضى من الأفعال والأقوال، والبلوغ إلى كل مرتقى من الفضائل والآداب، وجعلت الحروب للتألف بُعد عن إصابته بسائر أسباب التألف من المحاجات وأنواع البر. ولذلك – والله أعلم – أخر (الله) فرض الجهاد والقتال عن سائر أنواع الفرائض حتى ينتهي أسباب التأليف والتفريق لها ثم تظهر المكابرات للعقول، والمعاندات للحق، وتزول منفعة المحاجة وأنواع البر واللطف فوضع القتال ليكون التألف بذلك، ولذلك عظم الله مننه على الخلق بتأليف القلوب فقال : ( وَأَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ لَوْ أَنفَقْتَ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا مَّا الْفَتَّ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ الله أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ ) وقال : فَأَصْبَحْتُم بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانَا ) الآية أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ فإذا كان التأليف موجودًا بدون الحرب وإراقة الدماء، وتغلب على ذلك الطمع بما يعرفه من سآمة الفريقين، وما يظهر من آثار طلب الراحة منهم، والظفر بالأمن كانت الحكمة في الاشتغال به لتندفع معرة القتال وتتألف القلوب وتتحد الكلمة، فعلي له لما عاين آثار السامة في القوم رجا أن يحصل تألف القلوب بالتحكيم، واشتغل به وهو الغاية من الحكمة والنهاية فى الشفقة والمرحمة على الأمة على رجاء منه أن يصيب من أسندت إليه الحكومة الحق ويظفر بالثواب، فيكون في ذلك البلوغ إلى ما جعلت له الحروب على المسالمة والمصالحة اقتداء بما أمر الله تعالى من نصب الحكمين في الاختلاف بين الزوجين وما نصب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الحكمين في اختلاف وقع بينه وبين أهل مكة، وما جرى من الاصطلاح، فالأمة التي جاءت فيهم الشهادة عن الله تعالى بالآخرة وأمر الدين الذي عظم أمره التدبر والنظر، والإمامة التي المقصود منها التأليف والأمن أحق أن يعمل لها ذلك، ثم هؤلاء لما أقروا بالإمامة والخلافة وعلموا بالأسباب التي ظهرت لهم من نفسه مما صلح بها للخلافة، ثم لم تكن تغيرت تلك في نفسه ولا تبدلت ثم كان التحكيم منه حكما حكم به بسبب الإمامة فيلزمهم بحق إمامته القبول منه وإن ضاق عليهم وجه معرفة عذره في ذلك، ثم العجب من غباوة الخوارج أنهم خطأوه في التحكيم، ولو أنهم جعلوا ذلك حجة لهم عليه فيما كان من قبل، إذ كيف لم يبدأ بالمصالحة ثم كان يرجع إلى الحروب كان أقرب من أن جعلوا الأمر الأول من الحروب دلالة على
[On the issue of arbitration] As for the discussion on arbitration, our scholars and all Ahl al-Sunna hold that Ali was correct in the arbitration, while the Khawarij claimed that he was mistaken in it and had disbelieved, because the obligation toward the aggressors is to fight, as God said: 'But if one of them transgresses against the other, then fight the one that transgresses until it returns to the command of God.' However, our scholars—may God have mercy on them—said: This is the statement of one who is ignorant of the wisdom of the imamate and the greatness of its status in matters of religion and politics. For the wisdom of the imamate is only apparent and its status is great because of what it contains of bringing creatures together and uniting hearts, which are the cause of security and survival, and through them fulfillment is achieved in every approved action and word, and reaching every peak of virtues and manners. Fighting is made for unity, distant from attaining it through other means of unity such as arguments and types of goodness. Therefore—and God knows best—God delayed the obligation of jihad and fighting from other types of obligations until the means of unity and division were exhausted, then stubbornness toward intellects and obstinacy against truth appear, and the benefit of argumentation and types of goodness and kindness vanish, so fighting was placed so that unity might be achieved through it. For that reason, God made great His favor upon the creation by uniting hearts, saying: 'And He united their hearts; if you had spent all that is in the earth, you could not have united their hearts, but God united them,' and He said: 'Thus you became, by His favor, brothers.' So if unity can exist without war and bloodshed, and greed overcomes it by what one knows of the weariness of the two parties and what appears from signs of seeking comfort and achieving security, then the wisdom lies in occupying oneself with it to repel the disgrace of fighting and to unite hearts and make the word one. So Ali, when he saw signs of weariness among the people, hoped that unity of hearts could be achieved through arbitration, and he occupied himself with it—and that is the ultimate wisdom and the extreme of compassion and mercy toward the Ummah, hoping that the one to whom the judgment was entrusted would hit upon the truth and attain reward. In that is the attainment of what fighting was established for: peace and reconciliation, following the command of God to appoint two arbitrators in disputes between spouses, and what the Messenger of God appointed two arbitrators in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what happened of reconciliation. So the community about whom God gave testimony of the Hereafter and the matter of religion, whose importance is great deliberation and reflection, and the imamate whose purpose is unity and security, is more deserving that this be done for it. Then when these people acknowledged the imamate and caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his character that made him suitable for the caliphate, and then those reasons did not change in him nor alter, then the arbitration was a judgment he made by virtue of the imamate, so it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept it from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse is narrow for them. Then amazing is the foolishness of the Khawarij that they declared him wrong in the arbitration. If they had made that a proof against him regarding what was before, how did he not begin with reconciliation and then revert to fighting? It would have been nearer than making the first action of fighting an indication...
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a sustained refutation of the Khawarij position that Ali erred by agreeing to arbitration. The author begins by stating the Sunni position that Ali was correct, and the Khawarij claim that he was mistaken and became an unbeliever because the Quran commands fighting until the aggressor returns to God's command. The author then argues that this objection stems from ignorance of the wisdom of imamate. The purpose of imamate is to unite hearts and bring security. Fighting itself is only a means for unity, and it is deferred until other means fail. God emphasizes unity of hearts. If unity can be achieved without war, as when Ali saw weariness in the camps, it is wiser to pursue arbitration. The author supports this with Quranic verses about family arbitration and the Prophet's own arbitration with the Quraysh. Furthermore, since the opponents acknowledged Ali's imamate and his qualifications, they are obligated to accept his judgment. Finally, the author points out the inconsistency of the Khawarij: if they argue that Ali should have sought reconciliation before war, then they should criticize his initial war, not the arbitration. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing with further critique.

Key Terms
التحكيم
الخوارج
أهل السنة
الإمامة
التأليف
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Arbitration is a sign of weakness or error in leadership.
Correction: Arbitration is an application of the imamate's purpose to achieve unity without bloodshed, as seen in Quranic and prophetic examples.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the primary purpose of the imamate?
A) To wage war against aggressors
B) To unite hearts and bring security
C) To enforce religious law
D) To collect taxes

Key Takeaway
Ali's arbitration was not an error but a wise implementation of the imamate's fundamental goal of unity and security.

Refutation of the Khawarij's Objection to Arbitration
Author refutes Khawarij by highlighting their inconsistency and obligation to accept the imam's judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of the Khawarij argument that Ali erred in arbitration, based on the obligation to accept the imam's judgment and the inconsistency of their position.

Core Idea
Those who accepted Ali's imamate must accept his judgment; Khawarij are inconsistent.

Having established the wisdom of arbitration, the author now directly refutes the Khawarij. He argues that since the Khawarij acknowledged Ali's imamate and his qualifications, they are bound to accept his decisions. Moreover, their criticism is self-defeating: if they claim he should have sought reconciliation earlier, then they should criticize his initial fighting, not the arbitration.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation argument
The author points out that the Khawarij acknowledged Ali's imamate and his suitability for leadership. Therefore, they must accept his judgment in arbitration.
This is a point about consistency and the authority of the imam.
2
Understand the inconsistency
The author finds it foolish that the Khawarij criticize the arbitration but not the initial war. If they argue that reconciliation should come first, then they should have objected to the war, not the peace.
The Arabic uses 'غباوة' (foolishness) to describe their stance.
3
Reflect on the broader principle
This lesson shows that theological arguments must be consistent and that the authority of the imam must be respected in matters of public policy.

Source Text

الله تعالى: ﴿ فَإِنْ بَغَتْ إِحْدَتهُمَا عَلَى الْأُخْرَىٰ فَقَتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي حَتَّى تَفِيءَ إِلَى أَمْرِ الله ) الآية، ولكن أصحابنا – رحمهم الله – قالوا: إن هذا قول من جهل حكمة الإمامة وعظم منزلتهما في أمر الدين والسياسة، فإن حكمة الإمامة إنما جلت ومنزلتها عظمت بما فيها من تألف الخلق واجتماع القلوب اللذين هما سبب الأمن والبقاء، وبهما الوفاء في كل مرتضى من الأفعال والأقوال، والبلوغ إلى كل مرتقى من الفضائل والآداب، وجعلت الحروب للتألف بُعد عن إصابته بسائر أسباب التألف من المحاجات وأنواع البر. ولذلك – والله أعلم – أخر (الله) فرض الجهاد والقتال عن سائر أنواع الفرائض حتى ينتهي أسباب التأليف والتفريق لها ثم تظهر المكابرات للعقول، والمعاندات للحق، وتزول منفعة المحاجة وأنواع البر واللطف فوضع القتال ليكون التألف بذلك، ولذلك عظم الله مننه على الخلق بتأليف القلوب فقال : ( وَأَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ لَوْ أَنفَقْتَ مَا فِي الْأَرْضِ جَمِيعًا مَّا الْفَتَّ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ الله أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ ) وقال : فَأَصْبَحْتُم بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانَا ) الآية أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ فإذا كان التأليف موجودًا بدون الحرب وإراقة الدماء، وتغلب على ذلك الطمع بما يعرفه من سآمة الفريقين، وما يظهر من آثار طلب الراحة منهم، والظفر بالأمن كانت الحكمة في الاشتغال به لتندفع معرة القتال وتتألف القلوب وتتحد الكلمة، فعلي له لما عاين آثار السامة في القوم رجا أن يحصل تألف القلوب بالتحكيم، واشتغل به وهو الغاية من الحكمة والنهاية فى الشفقة والمرحمة على الأمة على رجاء منه أن يصيب من أسندت إليه الحكومة الحق ويظفر بالثواب، فيكون في ذلك البلوغ إلى ما جعلت له الحروب على المسالمة والمصالحة اقتداء بما أمر الله تعالى من نصب الحكمين في الاختلاف بين الزوجين وما نصب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الحكمين في اختلاف وقع بينه وبين أهل مكة، وما جرى من الاصطلاح، فالأمة التي جاءت فيهم الشهادة عن الله تعالى بالآخرة وأمر الدين الذي عظم أمره التدبر والنظر، والإمامة التي المقصود منها التأليف والأمن أحق أن يعمل لها ذلك، ثم هؤلاء لما أقروا بالإمامة والخلافة وعلموا بالأسباب التي ظهرت لهم من نفسه مما صلح بها للخلافة، ثم لم تكن تغيرت تلك في نفسه ولا تبدلت ثم كان التحكيم منه حكما حكم به بسبب الإمامة فيلزمهم بحق إمامته القبول منه وإن ضاق عليهم وجه معرفة عذره في ذلك، ثم العجب من غباوة الخوارج أنهم خطأوه في التحكيم، ولو أنهم جعلوا ذلك حجة لهم عليه فيما كان من قبل، إذ كيف لم يبدأ بالمصالحة ثم كان يرجع إلى الحروب كان أقرب من أن جعلوا الأمر الأول من الحروب دلالة على
[On the issue of arbitration] As for the discussion on arbitration, our scholars and all Ahl al-Sunna hold that Ali was correct in the arbitration, while the Khawarij claimed that he was mistaken in it and had disbelieved, because the obligation toward the aggressors is to fight, as God said: 'But if one of them transgresses against the other, then fight the one that transgresses until it returns to the command of God.' However, our scholars—may God have mercy on them—said: This is the statement of one who is ignorant of the wisdom of the imamate and the greatness of its status in matters of religion and politics. For the wisdom of the imamate is only apparent and its status is great because of what it contains of bringing creatures together and uniting hearts, which are the cause of security and survival, and through them fulfillment is achieved in every approved action and word, and reaching every peak of virtues and manners. Fighting is made for unity, distant from attaining it through other means of unity such as arguments and types of goodness. Therefore—and God knows best—God delayed the obligation of jihad and fighting from other types of obligations until the means of unity and division were exhausted, then stubbornness toward intellects and obstinacy against truth appear, and the benefit of argumentation and types of goodness and kindness vanish, so fighting was placed so that unity might be achieved through it. For that reason, God made great His favor upon the creation by uniting hearts, saying: 'And He united their hearts; if you had spent all that is in the earth, you could not have united their hearts, but God united them,' and He said: 'Thus you became, by His favor, brothers.' So if unity can exist without war and bloodshed, and greed overcomes it by what one knows of the weariness of the two parties and what appears from signs of seeking comfort and achieving security, then the wisdom lies in occupying oneself with it to repel the disgrace of fighting and to unite hearts and make the word one. So Ali, when he saw signs of weariness among the people, hoped that unity of hearts could be achieved through arbitration, and he occupied himself with it—and that is the ultimate wisdom and the extreme of compassion and mercy toward the Ummah, hoping that the one to whom the judgment was entrusted would hit upon the truth and attain reward. In that is the attainment of what fighting was established for: peace and reconciliation, following the command of God to appoint two arbitrators in disputes between spouses, and what the Messenger of God appointed two arbitrators in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what happened of reconciliation. So the community about whom God gave testimony of the Hereafter and the matter of religion, whose importance is great deliberation and reflection, and the imamate whose purpose is unity and security, is more deserving that this be done for it. Then when these people acknowledged the imamate and caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his character that made him suitable for the caliphate, and then those reasons did not change in him nor alter, then the arbitration was a judgment he made by virtue of the imamate, so it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept it from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse is narrow for them. Then amazing is the foolishness of the Khawarij that they declared him wrong in the arbitration. If they had made that a proof against him regarding what was before, how did he not begin with reconciliation and then revert to fighting? It would have been nearer than making the first action of fighting an indication...
Source pages p. 522

Commentary
This passage is a sustained refutation of the Khawarij position that Ali erred by agreeing to arbitration. The author begins by stating the Sunni position that Ali was correct, and the Khawarij claim that he was mistaken and became an unbeliever because the Quran commands fighting until the aggressor returns to God's command. The author then argues that this objection stems from ignorance of the wisdom of imamate. The purpose of imamate is to unite hearts and bring security. Fighting itself is only a means for unity, and it is deferred until other means fail. God emphasizes unity of hearts. If unity can be achieved without war, as when Ali saw weariness in the camps, it is wiser to pursue arbitration. The author supports this with Quranic verses about family arbitration and the Prophet's own arbitration with the Quraysh. Furthermore, since the opponents acknowledged Ali's imamate and his qualifications, they are obligated to accept his judgment. Finally, the author points out the inconsistency of the Khawarij: if they argue that Ali should have sought reconciliation before war, then they should criticize his initial war, not the arbitration. The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing with further critique.

الإمامة
التحكيم
غباوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can accept the imamate but reject the imam's specific judgments arbitrarily.
Correction: Accepting the imamate entails obligation to follow the imam's rulings, especially in matters like arbitration.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider the Khawarij foolish?
A) They did not accept Ali as caliph
B) They criticized arbitration but not the initial war
C) They refused to fight at all
D) They accepted arbitration too easily

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij are inconsistent: they accepted Ali's imamate but rejected his arbitration, and their criticism applies more strongly to his initial war than to his peace efforts.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you accepted someone's leadership but rejected their difficult decisions? What does this passage reveal about the inconsistency in your heart?
?
Are there areas where you apply stricter standards to others than to yourself, as the Khawarij did with Ali? How will you repent from this hypocrisy today?
?
The Khawarij insisted on their own reasoning over the imam's authority. Where in your life do you prioritize your own opinion over legitimate authority, and what will you do to submit?

Sects and Disagreements

The Wisdom and Precedents of Arbitration
Defense of arbitration using Quranic and prophetic precedents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends Ali's acceptance of arbitration by citing Quranic verses and prophetic precedents that prioritize unity over war.

Core Idea
Allah Himself unites hearts — arbitration follows divine precedent.

In this passage, the author addresses the Khawarij's main objection to Ali's arbitration by shifting the focus from the act of arbitration itself to its underlying purpose: achieving unity and avoiding bloodshed. Drawing on clear Quranic verses and the Prophet's own example at Hudaybiyyah, he shows that arbitration is not a sign of weakness but of wisdom and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic evidence
The author begins by quoting two verses that show Allah unites hearts (Q 8:63, 3:103). Notice how he uses these to establish that unity can exist without war.
These are foundational for the argument.
2
Understand the reasoning from weariness
He argues that when both parties are weary and desire peace, wisdom dictates pursuing arbitration to repel the harm of fighting. See how he describes Ali's observation of the troops' fatigue.
3
Examine the prophetic precedents
He then cites two precedents: Allah's command to appoint arbiters in marital disputes, and the Prophet's appointment of arbiters in the dispute with the Meccans (Hudaybiyyah). Ask yourself: why are these relevant?
The marital analogy is especially striking — if arbitration works for couples, why not for the ummah?
4
Apply to the imamate
The author concludes that the ummah and the imamate, whose very purpose is unity and security, are even more deserving of such measures. This is the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ (١) وَقَالَ: فَأَصْبَحْتُم بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانًا (٢) الْآيَةَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ. فَإِذَا كَانَ التَّأْلِيفُ مَوْجُودًا بِدُونِ الْحَرْبِ وَإِرَاقَةِ الدِّمَاءِ، وَتَغَلَّبَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الطَّمَعُ بِمَا يَعْرِفُهُ مِنْ سَآمَةِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ، وَمَا يَظْهَرُ مِنْ آثَارِ طَلَبِ الرَّاحَةِ (٣) مِنْهُمْ، وَالظَّفَرِ بِالْأَمْنِ كَانَتِ الْحِكْمَةُ فِي الِاشْتِغَالِ (٤) بِهِ لِتَنْدَفِعَ مَعَرَّةُ الْقِتَالِ وَتَتَأَلَّفَ الْقُلُوبُ وَتَتَّحِدَ الْكَلِمَةُ. فَعَلِيٌّ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ لَمَّا عَايَنَ آثَارَ السَّآمَةِ فِي الْقَوْمِ رَجَا أَنْ يَحْصُلَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ، وَاشْتَغَلَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَايَةُ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالنِّهَايَةُ فِي الشَّفَقَةِ وَالْمَرْحَمَةِ عَلَى الْأُمَّةِ عَلَى رَجَاءٍ مِنْهُ أَنْ يُصِيبَ مَنْ أُسْنِدَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْحُكُومَةُ الْحَقَّ وَيَظْفَرَ بِالثَّوَابِ، فَيَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ الْبُلُوغُ إِلَى مَا جُعِلَتْ لَهُ الْحُرُوبُ عَلَى الْمُسَالَمَةِ وَالْمُصَالَحَةِ اقْتِدَاءً بِمَا أَمَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَصْبِ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي الِاخْتِلَافِ بَيْنَ الزَّوْجَيْنِ، وَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي اخْتِلَافٍ وَقَعَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ، وَمَا جَرَى مِنَ الِاصْطِلَاحِ. فَالْأُمَّةُ الَّتِي جَاءَتْ فِيهِمُ الشَّهَادَةُ عَنِ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِالْآخِرَةِ وَأَمْرُ الدِّينِ الَّذِي عَظُمَ أَمْرُهُ التَّدَبُّرُ وَالنَّظَرُ، وَالْإِمَامَةُ الَّتِي الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهَا التَّأْلِيفُ وَالْأَمْنُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ يُعْمَلَ لَهَا ذَلِكَ. ثُمَّ هَؤُلَاءِ لَمَّا أَقَرُّوا بِالْإِمَامَةِ وَالْخِلَافَةِ وَعَلِمُوا بِالْأَسْبَابِ الَّتِي ظَهَرَتْ لَهُمْ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ (٩) مِمَّا صَلُحَ بِهَا لِلْخِلَافَةِ، ثُمَّ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَغَيَّرَتْ تِلْكَ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَبَدَّلَتْ، ثُمَّ كَانَ التَّحْكِيمُ مِنْهُ حُكْمًا حَكَمَ بِهِ بِسَبَبِ الْإِمَامَةِ فَيَلْزَمُهُمْ بِحَقِّ إِمَامَتِهِ الْقَبُولُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ ضَاقَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَجْهُ مَعْرِفَةِ عُذْرِهِ فِي ذَلِكَ. ثُمَّ الْعَجَبُ مِنْ غَبَاوَةِ الْخَوَارِجِ أَنَّهُمْ خَطَّأُوهُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ، وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ جَعَلُوا ذَلِكَ حُجَّةً لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ فِيمَا كَانَ (٦) مِنْ قَبْلُ، إِذْ كَيْفَ لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالْمُصَالَحَةِ ثُمَّ كَانَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْحُرُوبِ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ مِنْ أَنْ جَعَلُوا الْأَمْرَ الْأَوَّلَ مِنَ الْحُرُوبِ دَلَالَةً عَلَى غَيْرِ خَطَئِهِ فِي الثَّانِي، وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ فَاحِشَةٌ. وَتَعَلُّقُهُمْ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿ فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي ﴾ (١) مُسْتَقِيمٌ، لِأَنَّهُ ذُكِرَ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿ فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا ﴾ (٢) وَنَحْنُ كَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ الِاشْتِغَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ أَوَّلًا بِالدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الصُّلْحِ، ثُمَّ بَعْدَ وُقُوعِ الْيَأْسِ عَنِ الصُّلْحِ يُرْجَعُ إِلَى الْقِتَالِ لِيَحْصُلَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِذَلِكَ وَهُوَ تَأْلُفُ الْقُلُوبِ وَاجْتِمَاعُ الْكَلِمَةِ، وَاللهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ.
He united their hearts, but Allah united them. (1) And He said: 'And you became by His grace brothers.' (2) The verse: He united them. So if unity exists without war and bloodshed, and desire overcomes that due to what he knows of the weariness of the two parties, and what appears of traces of seeking comfort from them, and attaining security, then wisdom lies in engaging in it to repel the harm of fighting, and so that hearts become united and the word becomes one. Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when he saw the traces of weariness in the people, hoped that unity of hearts would be achieved through arbitration, and he occupied himself with it, and it is the ultimate wisdom and the utmost in compassion and mercy for the ummah, hoping that the one to whom arbitration was entrusted would attain the truth and succeed in reward, so that in that would be the attainment of what wars were made for: peace and reconciliation, following what Allah Almighty commanded regarding appointing two arbiters in disputes between spouses, and what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed two arbiters in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what occurred of reconciliation. So the ummah about whom testimony from Allah Almighty has come concerning the Hereafter, and the matter of religion whose importance is reflection and consideration, and the imamate whose purpose is unity and security, are more deserving that this be done for them. Then these people, when they acknowledged the imamate and the caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his own self (9) by which he was suitable for the caliphate, then those had not changed in his self nor altered, then the arbitration from him was a judgment he made due to the imamate, so it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse in that is difficult for them. Then the wonder is at the stupidity of the Khawarij: they considered him wrong in the arbitration. If only they had made that an argument against him regarding what was before, how did he not begin with reconciliation and then return to wars? That would be closer than making the first matter of wars an indication of something other than his error in the second. This is gross ignorance. And their clinging to His statement: 'Then fight the one that transgresses' (1) is valid, because it is mentioned after His statement: 'Then make peace between them' (2). And we likewise say: engagement should first be with calling to peace, then after despair of peace, one returns to fighting to achieve the purpose thereby, which is unity of hearts and gathering of the word. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Ali's acceptance of arbitration (tahkim) against the Khawarij's criticism. The author begins by citing two Quranic verses (Al-Anfal 63 and Al-Imran 103) which show that Allah Himself unites hearts, and that this unity can be achieved without war. He argues that since unity exists without war, and given the weariness of both sides and the desire for peace, it is wise to engage in arbitration to avoid the harm of fighting and to unite hearts. Ali observed this weariness and hoped arbitration would achieve unity, acting out of wisdom and mercy for the ummah. This follows the precedent of Allah commanding two arbiters in marital disputes and the Prophet appointing two arbiters with the Meccans at Hudaybiyyah. The ummah and the imamate, whose purpose is unity and security, are even more deserving of such measures. The author then points out the contradiction of the Khawarij: they acknowledged Ali's imamate and his suitability for it, but reject his judgment in arbitration. If they had used his initial wars as an argument against him, it would have been more consistent. Their interpretation of the verse 'fight the transgressor' is refuted because the verse itself begins with 'make peace'. The correct approach is to call to peace first, then fight only when peace is hopeless. Thus Ali's action was correct.

Key Terms
تحكيم
تأليف القلوب
مصالحة
حكمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Arbitration (tahkim) is a sign of weakness or a mistake on Ali's part.
Correction: The author shows that arbitration is a Quranic and prophetic practice aimed at achieving unity and avoiding bloodshed, and that Ali's action was wise and merciful.

Checkpoint
Which two precedents does the author cite to support the legitimacy of arbitration?
A) The arbitration between the Ansar and Muhajirun, and the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah.
B) The appointment of arbiters in marital disputes (Quran) and the Prophet's arbitration with the Meccans (Hudaybiyyah).
C) The arbitration of Abu Bakr and Umar, and the arbitration of the Khawarij.
D) The arbitration of the two angels Harut and Marut, and the arbitration of the Prophet with the Jews.

Key Takeaway
Arbitration is a legitimate, divinely sanctioned means of achieving unity, and Ali's acceptance was an act of wisdom and mercy, not a mistake.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent disagreement where you insisted on your position. Did you pause to consider the weariness of the other party? If Ali could set aside his clear military advantage for the sake of unity, whose example are you following when you refuse to budge? Take one concrete step today to open a door of reconciliation.
?
You believe in Allah's power to unite hearts—but do you rely on that power, or do you cling to your grievances as if your anger holds more authority than divine grace? What would change if you truly trusted that Allah's unity is stronger than your rightness?
?
The Prophet accepted the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah against the emotional wishes of his companions. Where in your life are you demanding 'victory' when what is actually needed is humility? If you were to follow the Prophet's suma in that moment, what would you have to sacrifice—and is your ego worth more than the unity of the community?

Refutation of the Khawarij's Objections
Refutation of Khawarij's logical and scriptural objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation of the Khawarij's two main arguments: that Ali's arbitration contradicts their acknowledgment of his imamate, and that the Quranic command to fight the transgressor should have been followed instead.

Core Idea
The Khawarij's criticism is self-defeating — they accepted Ali's imamate but reject his ruling.

Having established the legitimacy of arbitration, the author now turns to dismantle the Khawarij's specific objections. He points out the logical contradiction in their position: they recognized Ali's suitability for the caliphate but refuse to accept his judgment. He also addresses their proof-texting of the verse 'fight the transgressor' by showing that it is preceded by the command to make peace.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contradiction
The author notes that the Khawarij had acknowledged Ali's imamate and the reasons that made him suitable. Since arbitration was a judgment made by virtue of his imamate, they must accept it. Ask yourself: why is this a strong argument?
The logic is: if you accept the authority, you accept its decisions.
2
Understand the alternative criticism
He then points out that if the Khawarij wanted to criticize, they should have argued that Ali should have started with reconciliation before war, not that war before arbitration was wrong. This shows their 'gross ignorance'.
They criticized the wrong thing.
3
Analyze the verse interpretation
The Khawarij cling to 'fight the transgressor', but the author shows that the verse itself places peace first. The proper sequence is: call to peace, then fight only if peace fails. This disarms their proof.
He uses the very verse they cite to refute them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَلَّفَ بَيْنَ قُلُوبِهِمْ وَلَكِنَّ اللهَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ (١) وَقَالَ: فَأَصْبَحْتُم بِنِعْمَتِهِ إِخْوَانًا (٢) الْآيَةَ أَلَّفَ بَيْنَهُمْ. فَإِذَا كَانَ التَّأْلِيفُ مَوْجُودًا بِدُونِ الْحَرْبِ وَإِرَاقَةِ الدِّمَاءِ، وَتَغَلَّبَ عَلَى ذَلِكَ الطَّمَعُ بِمَا يَعْرِفُهُ مِنْ سَآمَةِ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ، وَمَا يَظْهَرُ مِنْ آثَارِ طَلَبِ الرَّاحَةِ (٣) مِنْهُمْ، وَالظَّفَرِ بِالْأَمْنِ كَانَتِ الْحِكْمَةُ فِي الِاشْتِغَالِ (٤) بِهِ لِتَنْدَفِعَ مَعَرَّةُ الْقِتَالِ وَتَتَأَلَّفَ الْقُلُوبُ وَتَتَّحِدَ الْكَلِمَةُ. فَعَلِيٌّ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ لَمَّا عَايَنَ آثَارَ السَّآمَةِ فِي الْقَوْمِ رَجَا أَنْ يَحْصُلَ تَأَلُّفُ الْقُلُوبِ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ، وَاشْتَغَلَ بِهِ وَهُوَ الْغَايَةُ مِنَ الْحِكْمَةِ وَالنِّهَايَةُ فِي الشَّفَقَةِ وَالْمَرْحَمَةِ عَلَى الْأُمَّةِ عَلَى رَجَاءٍ مِنْهُ أَنْ يُصِيبَ مَنْ أُسْنِدَتْ إِلَيْهِ الْحُكُومَةُ الْحَقَّ وَيَظْفَرَ بِالثَّوَابِ، فَيَكُونَ فِي ذَلِكَ الْبُلُوغُ إِلَى مَا جُعِلَتْ لَهُ الْحُرُوبُ عَلَى الْمُسَالَمَةِ وَالْمُصَالَحَةِ اقْتِدَاءً بِمَا أَمَرَ اللهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَصْبِ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي الِاخْتِلَافِ بَيْنَ الزَّوْجَيْنِ، وَمَا نَصَبَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ الْحَكَمَيْنِ فِي اخْتِلَافٍ وَقَعَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ، وَمَا جَرَى مِنَ الِاصْطِلَاحِ. فَالْأُمَّةُ الَّتِي جَاءَتْ فِيهِمُ الشَّهَادَةُ عَنِ اللهِ تَعَالَى بِالْآخِرَةِ وَأَمْرُ الدِّينِ الَّذِي عَظُمَ أَمْرُهُ التَّدَبُّرُ وَالنَّظَرُ، وَالْإِمَامَةُ الَّتِي الْمَقْصُودُ مِنْهَا التَّأْلِيفُ وَالْأَمْنُ أَحَقُّ أَنْ يُعْمَلَ لَهَا ذَلِكَ. ثُمَّ هَؤُلَاءِ لَمَّا أَقَرُّوا بِالْإِمَامَةِ وَالْخِلَافَةِ وَعَلِمُوا بِالْأَسْبَابِ الَّتِي ظَهَرَتْ لَهُمْ مِنْ نَفْسِهِ (٩) مِمَّا صَلُحَ بِهَا لِلْخِلَافَةِ، ثُمَّ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَغَيَّرَتْ تِلْكَ فِي نَفْسِهِ وَلَا تَبَدَّلَتْ، ثُمَّ كَانَ التَّحْكِيمُ مِنْهُ حُكْمًا حَكَمَ بِهِ بِسَبَبِ الْإِمَامَةِ فَيَلْزَمُهُمْ بِحَقِّ إِمَامَتِهِ الْقَبُولُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ ضَاقَ عَلَيْهِمْ وَجْهُ مَعْرِفَةِ عُذْرِهِ فِي ذَلِكَ. ثُمَّ الْعَجَبُ مِنْ غَبَاوَةِ الْخَوَارِجِ أَنَّهُمْ خَطَّأُوهُ فِي التَّحْكِيمِ، وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ جَعَلُوا ذَلِكَ حُجَّةً لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِ فِيمَا كَانَ (٦) مِنْ قَبْلُ، إِذْ كَيْفَ لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالْمُصَالَحَةِ ثُمَّ كَانَ يَرْجِعُ إِلَى الْحُرُوبِ كَانَ أَقْرَبَ مِنْ أَنْ جَعَلُوا الْأَمْرَ الْأَوَّلَ مِنَ الْحُرُوبِ دَلَالَةً عَلَى غَيْرِ خَطَئِهِ فِي الثَّانِي، وَهَذِهِ جَهَالَةٌ فَاحِشَةٌ. وَتَعَلُّقُهُمْ بِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿ فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي ﴾ (١) مُسْتَقِيمٌ، لِأَنَّهُ ذُكِرَ بَعْدَ قَوْلِهِ: ﴿ فَأَصْلِحُوا بَيْنَهُمَا ﴾ (٢) وَنَحْنُ كَذَا نَقُولُ: إِنَّ الِاشْتِغَالَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ يَكُونَ أَوَّلًا بِالدُّعَاءِ إِلَى الصُّلْحِ، ثُمَّ بَعْدَ وُقُوعِ الْيَأْسِ عَنِ الصُّلْحِ يُرْجَعُ إِلَى الْقِتَالِ لِيَحْصُلَ الْمَقْصُودُ بِذَلِكَ وَهُوَ تَأْلُفُ الْقُلُوبِ وَاجْتِمَاعُ الْكَلِمَةِ، وَاللهُ الْمُوَفِّقُ.
He united their hearts, but Allah united them. (1) And He said: 'And you became by His grace brothers.' (2) The verse: He united them. So if unity exists without war and bloodshed, and desire overcomes that due to what he knows of the weariness of the two parties, and what appears of traces of seeking comfort from them, and attaining security, then wisdom lies in engaging in it to repel the harm of fighting, and so that hearts become united and the word becomes one. Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) when he saw the traces of weariness in the people, hoped that unity of hearts would be achieved through arbitration, and he occupied himself with it, and it is the ultimate wisdom and the utmost in compassion and mercy for the ummah, hoping that the one to whom arbitration was entrusted would attain the truth and succeed in reward, so that in that would be the attainment of what wars were made for: peace and reconciliation, following what Allah Almighty commanded regarding appointing two arbiters in disputes between spouses, and what the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed two arbiters in a dispute that occurred between him and the people of Mecca, and what occurred of reconciliation. So the ummah about whom testimony from Allah Almighty has come concerning the Hereafter, and the matter of religion whose importance is reflection and consideration, and the imamate whose purpose is unity and security, are more deserving that this be done for them. Then these people, when they acknowledged the imamate and the caliphate and knew the reasons that appeared to them from his own self (9) by which he was suitable for the caliphate, then those had not changed in his self nor altered, then the arbitration from him was a judgment he made due to the imamate, so it is incumbent upon them by right of his imamate to accept from him, even if the way of knowing his excuse in that is difficult for them. Then the wonder is at the stupidity of the Khawarij: they considered him wrong in the arbitration. If only they had made that an argument against him regarding what was before, how did he not begin with reconciliation and then return to wars? That would be closer than making the first matter of wars an indication of something other than his error in the second. This is gross ignorance. And their clinging to His statement: 'Then fight the one that transgresses' (1) is valid, because it is mentioned after His statement: 'Then make peace between them' (2). And we likewise say: engagement should first be with calling to peace, then after despair of peace, one returns to fighting to achieve the purpose thereby, which is unity of hearts and gathering of the word. And Allah is the Giver of success.
Source pages p. 523

Commentary
This passage is a defense of Ali's acceptance of arbitration (tahkim) against the Khawarij's criticism. The author begins by citing two Quranic verses (Al-Anfal 63 and Al-Imran 103) which show that Allah Himself unites hearts, and that this unity can be achieved without war. He argues that since unity exists without war, and given the weariness of both sides and the desire for peace, it is wise to engage in arbitration to avoid the harm of fighting and to unite hearts. Ali observed this weariness and hoped arbitration would achieve unity, acting out of wisdom and mercy for the ummah. This follows the precedent of Allah commanding two arbiters in marital disputes and the Prophet appointing two arbiters with the Meccans at Hudaybiyyah. The ummah and the imamate, whose purpose is unity and security, are even more deserving of such measures. The author then points out the contradiction of the Khawarij: they acknowledged Ali's imamate and his suitability for it, but reject his judgment in arbitration. If they had used his initial wars as an argument against him, it would have been more consistent. Their interpretation of the verse 'fight the transgressor' is refuted because the verse itself begins with 'make peace'. The correct approach is to call to peace first, then fight only when peace is hopeless. Thus Ali's action was correct.

Key Terms
خوارج
إمامة
غباوة
جهالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'fight the transgressor' commands immediate military action against a rebellious faction without prior peace efforts.
Correction: The author shows that the verse is preceded by 'make peace', so the proper sequence is call to peace, then fight only after despair of peace.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the proper sequence for dealing with conflict between Muslim groups?
A) Fight first to establish authority, then make peace afterward.
B) Call to peace first, then fight only after despair of peace.
C) Immediately appoint arbiters and avoid fighting altogether.
D) Always fight until one side submits, as the verse commands.

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij's criticism of Ali's arbitration is logically inconsistent and scripturally unfounded, as peace must always be the first resort.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disagree with a leader or scholar you once respected, do you examine your own reasoning for inconsistency before condemning theirs? What would it cost you to admit you might be wrong, even if their action is hard to understand?
?
This lesson shows that the Khawarij clung to a valid Quranic verse but ignored its context. Where in your life do you selectively use religious texts to support a position while neglecting other commands? How will you correct this today?
?
The author calls the Khawarij's criticism 'gross ignorance'. Have you ever been certain you were right about a religious matter, only later to realize your argument was self-defeating? What step will you take to avoid that kind of blindness in the future?
