Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
8 min
The Inconsistency of the Khawarij
Dialectical refutation of Khawarij via their own actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses a dialectical dilemma to expose the Khawarij's inconsistency in accusing Ali of disbelief while they themselves delayed fighting him.

Core Idea
The Khawarij's own actions condemn them if Ali is a disbeliever.

This passage presents a powerful refutation of the Khawarij by turning their own logic against them. The author forces them to confront a dilemma: if they delayed fighting Ali to debate him, does that make them disbelievers? Their answer reveals their inconsistency.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the author structures the argument as a series of conditional questions.
The dilemma is presented very systematically.
2
Trace the logical branches
Identify each possible answer the Khawarij might give and the consequence. Start from the first question and follow the 'if yes/no' possibilities.
This is a classic dialectical (jadal) technique.
3
Connect to Ali's arbitration
See how the author finally parallels the Khawarij's excuse with Ali's reason for arbitration. This shows the argument applies equally to both sides.
The author even mentions that Ali himself used this argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُقَالُ لِلْخَوَارِجِ: إِذَا اشْتَغَلْتُم بِمُنَاظَرَةِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ بِمُنَاظَرَةِ عَلِيٍّ - رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا - وَدَعَوْتُمُوهُمَا إِلَى مَا اعْتَقَدْتُمْ، وَتَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُ فِي تِلْكَ الْمُدَّةِ رَجَاءَ أَنْ يَعُودَ إِلَى رَأْيِكُمْ أَكْفَرْتُم بِذَلِكَ أَمْ لَا؟ فَإِن قَالُوا: نَعَمْ فَقَدْ (٣) أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِم بِالْكُفْرِ، وَإِن قَالُوا: لَا. قِيلَ: أَفَكُنْتُمْ فِي ذَلِكَ مُخْطِئِينَ أَمْ مُصِيبِينَ؟ فَإِن قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُخْطِئِينَ. فَقَدْ أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِم بِالْخَطَأِ وَهُوَ كُفْرٌ عِنْدَهُمْ، وَإِن قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُصِيبِينَ (٤). قِيلَ: وَلِمَ كُنْتُمْ كَذَلِكَ وَقَدْ تَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُ مُدَّةَ مُنَاظَرَتِكُمْ إِيَّاهُ () وَهُوَ كَافِرٌ فَكَذَلِكَ عَلِيٌّ لَا يَصِيرُ كَافِرًا بِتَرْكِهِ مُقَاتَلَةَ أُولَئِكَ؟ فَإِن قَالُوا: إِنَّا تَرَكْنَا قِتَالَنَا رَجَاءَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَهُوَ رُجُوعُهُ إِلَى الْحَقِّ بِدُونِ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْمُقَاتَلَةِ. قِيلَ: فَكَذَا عَلِيٌّ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ اشْتَغَلَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ لِهَذَا، وَحُكِيَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا احْتَجَّ عَلَيْهِم بِهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ سَبَبَ رُجُوعِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْهُمْ (٦) عَنْ (٧) ضَلَالَتِهِ. مَا يَحْكُونَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا شَكَّ فِي نَفْسِهِ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَصِفْهَا بِإِمْرَةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَأَجَابَهُمْ وَقْتَ التَّحْكِيمِ إِلَى أَن لَا يُكْتَبَ عَلَى أَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ. كَلَامٌ فَاسِدٌ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَشُكَّ فِي ذَلِكَ بَلْ أَرَادَ بِذَلِكَ حَسْمَ الشَّغَبِ، وَقَدْ فَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ فِي صُلْحِ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ حَيْثُ مَحَى اسْمَ رَسُولِ اللهِ وَقَالَ: أَنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ وَلَوْ أَبَيْتَ فَاكْتُبْ: ابْنُ عَبْدِ اللهِ.
And it is said to the Khawarij: When you engaged in debate with Ibn Abbas and then after that with Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) and called them both to what you believed, and you left off fighting him during that period hoping that he would return to your opinion, did you thereby become disbelievers or not? If they say: Yes, then they have admitted to disbelief against themselves. And if they say: No, it is said: Were you in that mistaken or correct? If they say: We were mistaken, then they have admitted error against themselves, and error is disbelief according to them. And if they say: We were correct, it is said: Why were you thus, and you left off fighting him during the period of your debating with him, and he is a disbeliever? So similarly, Ali does not become a disbeliever by leaving off fighting those people? If they say: We left off our fighting hoping for attainment of the purpose, which is his return to the truth without need for fighting. It is said: Similarly, Ali, except that he engaged in arbitration for this reason. And it is narrated that Ali argued against them with this very argument, and that was the cause of many of them returning from their misguidance. (6) (7) What they narrate that Ali doubted himself because he did not describe himself as 'Commander of the Faithful' and responded to them at the time of arbitration to not write 'Commander of the Faithful'. This is corrupt speech. For he did not doubt in that, but rather intended thereby to cut off disturbance. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did the same in the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah when he erased the name 'Messenger of Allah' and said: 'I am the Messenger of Allah, but if you refuse, write: Ibn Abdullah.'
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical refutation of the Khawarij. The author first poses a dilemma: the Khawarij themselves delayed fighting Ali to debate and persuade him; does that make them disbelievers? If they say yes, they condemn themselves. If no, then were they correct or mistaken? If mistaken, that is disbelief by their own standards; if correct, then why can Ali not similarly delay fighting for a legitimate purpose? The Khawarij might respond that they delayed hoping for his return to truth without fighting. The author retorts that this is exactly what Ali did by arbitration. The author then mentions that Ali himself used this argument, causing many Khawarij to repent. Finally, the author addresses a rumor that Ali doubted his own position because he agreed to drop the title 'Commander of the Faithful' from the arbitration document. The author dismisses this as corrupt speech, explaining that Ali did so to prevent strife, just as the Prophet did at Hudaybiyyah when he agreed to remove 'Messenger of Allah' and write his patronymic instead.

Key Terms
معضلة
تناقض
تحكيم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Khawarij believed they were consistent in condemning Ali for delaying fighting, while they themselves never delayed.
Correction: Their own delay in debating and hoping for his return proves that delay for a good reason does not constitute disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the Khawarij say they were mistaken in delaying fighting Ali?
A) They admit error, which they consider disbelief.
B) They are excused because they were seeking truth.
C) They must immediately fight him.
D) They become correct in their stance.

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij's own practice of delaying fighting for debate undermines their claim that Ali's delay for arbitration made him a disbeliever.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself critical of someone’s mistake, do you apply the same standard to your own actions? This passage forces you to see the Khawarij’s inconsistency. Where in your life are you holding others to a rule you don’t follow yourself?
?
The Khawarij delayed fighting to debate, yet condemned Ali for delaying to arbitrate. Have you ever condemned another for doing exactly what you yourself do, just with a different label? What would it take for you to see that inconsistency and repent from it today?
?
If the Khawarij were confronted with their own contradiction and many repented, what contradiction in your own faith practice have you been ignoring? This lesson demands you examine the gap between what you claim to believe and how you judge others. Will you let this argument pierce your heart and change your judgment?

The Wisdom of Ali's Omission of 'Amir al-Mu'minin'
Refutation of a rumor about Ali's doubt via prophetic precedent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ali agreed to drop the title 'Commander of the Faithful' and how the Prophet's precedent supports this action.

Core Idea
Ali's action followed the Prophet's precedent at Hudaybiyyah.

A rumor spread that Ali doubted his own position because he omitted the title 'Commander of the Faithful' from the arbitration document. The author refutes this by explaining Ali's true motive and invoking the Prophet's example in the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah.

Guided Path
1
Read the rumor and refutation
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the claim that Ali doubted himself because he agreed to drop his title.
This is a specific rumor the author addresses.
2
Understand Ali's true motive
The author explains that Ali did not doubt but rather sought to cut off disturbance (hasm al-shaghab).
This is a practical wisdom, not weakness.
3
Compare to Hudaybiyyah
The Prophet (peace be upon him) similarly erased his title from the treaty with the Quraysh, prioritizing peace over honorifics.
The parallel shows consistency with prophetic practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُقَالُ لِلْخَوَارِجِ: إِذَا اشْتَغَلْتُم بِمُنَاظَرَةِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ بِمُنَاظَرَةِ عَلِيٍّ - رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا - وَدَعَوْتُمُوهُمَا إِلَى مَا اعْتَقَدْتُمْ، وَتَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُ فِي تِلْكَ الْمُدَّةِ رَجَاءَ أَنْ يَعُودَ إِلَى رَأْيِكُمْ أَكْفَرْتُم بِذَلِكَ أَمْ لَا؟ فَإِن قَالُوا: نَعَمْ فَقَدْ (٣) أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِم بِالْكُفْرِ، وَإِن قَالُوا: لَا. قِيلَ: أَفَكُنْتُمْ فِي ذَلِكَ مُخْطِئِينَ أَمْ مُصِيبِينَ؟ فَإِن قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُخْطِئِينَ. فَقَدْ أَقَرُّوا عَلَى أَنفُسِهِم بِالْخَطَأِ وَهُوَ كُفْرٌ عِنْدَهُمْ، وَإِن قَالُوا: كُنَّا مُصِيبِينَ (٤). قِيلَ: وَلِمَ كُنْتُمْ كَذَلِكَ وَقَدْ تَرَكْتُمْ قِتَالَهُ مُدَّةَ مُنَاظَرَتِكُمْ إِيَّاهُ () وَهُوَ كَافِرٌ فَكَذَلِكَ عَلِيٌّ لَا يَصِيرُ كَافِرًا بِتَرْكِهِ مُقَاتَلَةَ أُولَئِكَ؟ فَإِن قَالُوا: إِنَّا تَرَكْنَا قِتَالَنَا رَجَاءَ حُصُولِ الْمَقْصُودِ وَهُوَ رُجُوعُهُ إِلَى الْحَقِّ بِدُونِ الْحَاجَةِ إِلَى الْمُقَاتَلَةِ. قِيلَ: فَكَذَا عَلِيٌّ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ اشْتَغَلَ بِالتَّحْكِيمِ لِهَذَا، وَحُكِيَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا احْتَجَّ عَلَيْهِم بِهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ، فَكَانَ ذَلِكَ سَبَبَ رُجُوعِ كَثِيرٍ مِنْهُمْ (٦) عَنْ (٧) ضَلَالَتِهِ. مَا يَحْكُونَ أَنَّ عَلِيًّا شَكَّ فِي نَفْسِهِ حَيْثُ لَمْ يَصِفْهَا بِإِمْرَةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَأَجَابَهُمْ وَقْتَ التَّحْكِيمِ إِلَى أَن لَا يُكْتَبَ عَلَى أَمِيرِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ. كَلَامٌ فَاسِدٌ، فَإِنَّهُ لَمْ يَشُكَّ فِي ذَلِكَ بَلْ أَرَادَ بِذَلِكَ حَسْمَ الشَّغَبِ، وَقَدْ فَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ فِي صُلْحِ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ حَيْثُ مَحَى اسْمَ رَسُولِ اللهِ وَقَالَ: أَنَا رَسُولُ اللهِ وَلَوْ أَبَيْتَ فَاكْتُبْ: ابْنُ عَبْدِ اللهِ.
And it is said to the Khawarij: When you engaged in debate with Ibn Abbas and then after that with Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both) and called them both to what you believed, and you left off fighting him during that period hoping that he would return to your opinion, did you thereby become disbelievers or not? If they say: Yes, then they have admitted to disbelief against themselves. And if they say: No, it is said: Were you in that mistaken or correct? If they say: We were mistaken, then they have admitted error against themselves, and error is disbelief according to them. And if they say: We were correct, it is said: Why were you thus, and you left off fighting him during the period of your debating with him, and he is a disbeliever? So similarly, Ali does not become a disbeliever by leaving off fighting those people? If they say: We left off our fighting hoping for attainment of the purpose, which is his return to the truth without need for fighting. It is said: Similarly, Ali, except that he engaged in arbitration for this reason. And it is narrated that Ali argued against them with this very argument, and that was the cause of many of them returning from their misguidance. (6) (7) What they narrate that Ali doubted himself because he did not describe himself as 'Commander of the Faithful' and responded to them at the time of arbitration to not write 'Commander of the Faithful'. This is corrupt speech. For he did not doubt in that, but rather intended thereby to cut off disturbance. And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did the same in the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah when he erased the name 'Messenger of Allah' and said: 'I am the Messenger of Allah, but if you refuse, write: Ibn Abdullah.'
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage presents a dialectical refutation of the Khawarij. The author first poses a dilemma: the Khawarij themselves delayed fighting Ali to debate and persuade him; does that make them disbelievers? If they say yes, they condemn themselves. If no, then were they correct or mistaken? If mistaken, that is disbelief by their own standards; if correct, then why can Ali not similarly delay fighting for a legitimate purpose? The Khawarij might respond that they delayed hoping for his return to truth without fighting. The author retorts that this is exactly what Ali did by arbitration. The author then mentions that Ali himself used this argument, causing many Khawarij to repent. Finally, the author addresses a rumor that Ali doubted his own position because he agreed to drop the title 'Commander of the Faithful' from the arbitration document. The author dismisses this as corrupt speech, explaining that Ali did so to prevent strife, just as the Prophet did at Hudaybiyyah when he agreed to remove 'Messenger of Allah' and write his patronymic instead.

شبهة
حذف اللقب
صُلْح
الْحُدَيْبِيَة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ali doubted his own legitimacy as caliph because he omitted his title from the document.
Correction: Ali did so intentionally to prevent strife, following the Prophet's example at Hudaybiyyah.

Checkpoint
What precedent does the author use to refute the rumor about Ali?
A) The Prophet's removal of his title at Hudaybiyyah.
B) Abu Bakr's refusal to negotiate.
C) Umar's insistence on using titles.
D) The Quranic verse on obedience.

Key Takeaway
Ali's omission of his title was not a sign of doubt but a wise decision to avoid conflict, following the Prophet's own example at Hudaybiyyah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you recall a time when you were misunderstood or accused of something, and you had the strength to respond with humility rather than demand recognition? How did that experience shape your character?
?
When your reputation or status is on the line, do you instinctively defend it, or do you weigh the higher good of unity and peace? What would it take for you to set aside a title or privilege for the sake of harmony, following the example of Ali and the Prophet?
?
If you were in a conflict where yielding a symbol of your authority could end the strife, would your faith in prophetic guidance be strong enough to make that choice, even if others might misinterpret it as weakness? What concrete step can you take today to emulate that kind of strategic wisdom?

Refutation of the Khawarij on Arbitration
Debate with Khawarij: analogy between arbitration and delaying combat for guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes the Khawarij by applying their own reasoning to their actions and by drawing a parallel to the Prophet's treaty.

Core Idea
The Khawarij's own practice justifies Ali's arbitration.

The Khawarij criticized Ali for agreeing to arbitration and for omitting his title. The author here presents a clever dialectical argument, showing that the Khawarij themselves postponed fighting for guidance, and that the Prophet set a similar precedent. This lesson walks through that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: first a question to the Khawarij, then a series of options, finally a response to the objection about the title.
The passage uses a dialectical method common in kalam.
2
Identify the key question and options
The author asks the Khawarij whether their own postponement of fighting to convince Ali was disbelief, error, or correct. Trace each option and its consequence.
The Khawarij's own rule condemns them if they admit error.
3
Examine the parallel with the Prophet
The author refutes the claim that Ali doubted his authority by citing the Prophet's treaty of Hudaybiyya, where the Prophet omitted his title to avoid strife.
This shows that Ali's action is not doubt but wisdom.
4
Understand the final point
Criticizing Ali on this matter implicitly criticizes the Prophet, which is tantamount to disbelief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مناقشة الخوارج في قولهم في التحكيم] ويقال للخوارج: إذا اشتغلتم بمناظرة ابن عباس ثم بعد ذلك بمناظرة علي رضي الله عنهما ودعوتهما إلى ما اعتقدتم، وتركتم قتاله في تلك المدة رجاء أن يعود إلى رأيكم أكفرتم بذلك أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: نعم فقد أقروا على أنفسهم بالكفر، وإن قالوا: لا. قيل: أفكنتم في ذلك مخطئين أم مصيبين؟ فإن قالوا: كنا مخطئين. فقد أقروا على أنفسهم بالخطأ وهو كفر عندهم، وإن قالوا: كنا مصيبين. قيل: ولم كنتم كذلك وقد تركتم قتاله مدة مناظرتكم إياه وهو كافر فكذلك علي لا يصير كافرًا بتركه مقاتلة أولئك؟ فإن قالوا: إنا تركنا قتالنا رجاء حصول المقصود وهو رجوعه إلى الحق بدون الحاجة إلى المقاتلة. قيل: فكذا علي الا انه اشتغل بالتحكيم لهذا، وحكي أن عليا احتج عليهم بهذا بعينه، فكان ذلك سبب رجوع كثير منهم عن ضلالته. ما يحكون أن عليا شك في نفسه حيث لم يصفها بإمرة المؤمنين وأجابهم وقت التحكيم إلى أن لا يكتب على أمير المؤمنين. كلام فاسد، فإنه لم يشك في ذلك بل أراد بذلك حسم الشغب، وقد فعل رسول الله عليه السلام مثل ذلك لما كتبت الموادعة بينه وبين سهيل بن عمرو فامتنع سهيل عن ذلك، وقال: لو أقررنا بأنك رسول الله ما قاتلناك، ولم يكن رسول الله عليه السلام شاكا في رسالة نفسه بل فعل قطعًا للشغب، وفي رسول الله عليه السلام أسوة حسنة، وهذا الطعن عائد على رسول الله عليه السلام وهو كفر، والله الموفق.
Discussion of the Khawarij regarding their statement on arbitration] And it is said to the Khawarij: When you engaged in disputation with Ibn Abbas and then after that with Ali - may Allah be pleased with both of them - and invited them to what you believed, and you left off fighting him during that period hoping that he would return to your opinion, did you thereby become disbelievers or not? If they say: Yes, then they have admitted against themselves disbelief. And if they say: No, it is said: Were you in that mistaken or correct? If they say: We were mistaken, then they have admitted against themselves error, and error constitutes disbelief according to them. And if they say: We were correct, it is said: Why were you so, while you left off fighting him for the duration of your disputation with him, and he was a disbeliever? So likewise Ali does not become a disbeliever by his leaving off fighting those people? If they say: We left off our fighting hoping for the attainment of the purpose, which is his return to the truth without need for fighting. It is said: So too with Ali, except that he occupied himself with arbitration for this reason. And it is narrated that Ali argued with them using this very argument, and that was the cause of many of them returning from their misguidance. As for what they narrate that Ali doubted himself when he did not describe himself as Commander of the Faithful and answered them at the time of arbitration by agreeing not to write 'Commander of the Faithful', this is corrupt speech. For he did not doubt in that, but rather intended by that to cut off sedition. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, did the like when the truce was written between him and Suhayl ibn Amr, and Suhayl refused that and said: If we acknowledged that you are the Messenger of Allah, we would not fight you. And the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was not doubtful about his own prophethood, but rather acted to cut off sedition. And in the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, there is a good example. And this criticism reflects back on the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, and it is disbelief. And Allah is the Granter of success.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Khawarij, specifically their stance on arbitration (tahkim). The author presents a dialectical argument against them. First, he asks the Khawarij about their own practice: when they disputed with Ibn Abbas and Ali, they postponed fighting Ali in the hope of convincing him. If they consider that postponement as disbelief, they condemn themselves; if not, they admit it was either error or correct. If error, they condemn themselves by their own rule; if correct, they must justify why Ali's postponement of fighting was also not correct. The Khawarij might argue they postponed fighting to achieve the purpose of guidance without force. The author then says that Ali similarly engaged in arbitration for the same reason, and Ali himself used this argument. Next, the author addresses the claim that Ali doubted himself by not insisting on the title 'Commander of the Faithful' during arbitration. The author refutes this as corrupt, explaining that Ali acted to prevent strife, just as the Prophet did when making the treaty of Hudaybiyya and omitting his title. The Prophet was not in doubt, so Ali was not. Criticizing Ali on this point implicitly criticizes the Prophet, which is disbelief.

Key Terms
الخوارج
التحكيم
الوقيعة
الشغب
أسوة حسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali doubted his own authority when he agreed not to write 'Commander of the Faithful' during arbitration.
Correction: Ali did not doubt; he acted to cut off sedition, following the Prophet's example in the treaty of Hudaybiyya.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the claim that Ali doubted himself?
A) By showing Ali later insisted on the title.
B) By citing the Prophet's similar action at Hudaybiyya.
C) By arguing that doubt is not disbelief.
D) By saying the Khawarij misinterpreted Ali's words.

Key Takeaway
The Khawarij's own actions and the Prophet's precedent refute their criticism of Ali's arbitration and omission of the title.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself dismissing a leader or scholar's decision because it seems weak or inconsistent, do you first examine your own actions for similar inconsistencies? Will you pause today to check if you condemn in others what you excuse in yourself?
?
The Prophet omitted his title for peace. Is there a title, label, or position you cling to that causes division? What would it cost you to set it aside for unity, and are you willing to pay that price before tomorrow?
?
The Khawarij's mistake was not just in their conclusion but in their assumption that their own intentions were pure while Ali's were flawed. How often do you assume bad faith in those you disagree with? What would change if you extended the same hope for guidance that you wish for yourself?

The Principle of Refraining from Reviling the Companions
Nasafi states the principle and gives two justifications for honoring Companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational principle of Ahl al-Sunna to refrain from reviling the Companions and the reasons why they are honored.

Core Idea
The Companions' sacrifices and transmission of religion demand our respect, not criticism.

This lesson introduces a core tenet of Sunni Islam: protecting the honor of the Companions. The author begins by stating the principle and then provides compelling reasons rooted in their unparalleled contributions to Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the principle
Read the first part of the passage where Nasafi states the principle of refraining from reviling the Companions and interpreting their affairs favorably.
Notice the phrase 'from the principles of Ahl al-Sunna'.
2
Identify the justifications
Identify the two main justifications given: the Companions' sacrifices and their role as transmitters of the religion.
3
Reflect on the honor
Consider how these justifications establish the elevated status of the Companions and why reviling them contradicts the Sunni approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلموا أن من أصول مذهب السنة والجماعة كف اللسان عن الوقيعة في الصحابة، وحمل أمرهم على ما يوجب دفع الطعن والقدح عنهم؛ إذ هم الذين بذلوا أنفسهم وأموالهم، وودعوا الدعة والراحة، وتحملوا المشاق العظيمة في نصرة دين الله تعالى وهم نقلة الدين إلى من بعدهم وهم المكرمون بصحبة خير البشر ونصرته وإيوائه ووقايته بأنفسهم والجود بمهجهم دونه، ولهذا جعل أبو حنيفة من شرائط السنة أن لا يحرم نبيذ الجر لما أن في تحريمه تفسيق كبار الصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - لما ثبت بطريق لا شبهة فيه شربهم نبيذ الجر، ولو كان محرما لأوجب لك فسقهم، فكان القول بحرمته موجبا تفسيقهم، والقول بتفسيقهم بدعة وخروج عن شرائط مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة.
Then know that among the principles of the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is restraining the tongue from reviling the Companions, and interpreting their affairs in a manner that necessitates repelling criticism and disparagement against them; for they are those who sacrificed themselves and their wealth, abandoned ease and comfort, and endured great hardships in supporting the religion of Allah Almighty, and they are the transmitters of the religion to those after them, and they are honored with the companionship of the best of mankind, and supporting him, giving him refuge, protecting him with their lives, and generously offering their souls for his sake. For this reason, Abu Hanifa made it among the conditions of the Sunna that one not declare nabidh al-jarr (date-wine) prohibited, because declaring it prohibited would entail declaring major Companions - may Allah be pleased with them - as sinners, since it is established by an unambiguous path that they drank nabidh al-jarr. Had it been prohibited, it would necessarily have necessitated their sinfulness. So the statement of its prohibition necessitates declaring them sinful, and declaring them sinful is an innovation and a departure from the conditions of the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage states a core principle of Ahl al-Sunna: refraining from reviling the Companions. The author gives two justifications: the Companions sacrificed everything for Islam and transmitted the religion, so they deserve honor. Then he provides a practical example from Abu Hanifa: making it a condition of the Sunna not to declare nabidh al-jarr prohibited, because doing so would necessitate declaring major Companions sinful since they drank it. Since declaring the Companions sinful is contrary to Ahl al-Sunna, the prohibition is rejected.

Key Terms
الوقيعة
الصحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think it is acceptable to criticize or revile the Companions because they were fallible humans.
Correction: This passage establishes that refraining from reviling them is a fundamental principle of Ahl al-Sunna, due to their unique sacrifices and role as transmitters of the religion.

Checkpoint
According to Nasafi, what is one reason the Companions should not be reviled?
A) They were all infallible prophets.
B) They sacrificed themselves and transmitted the religion.
C) They never made any mistakes.
D) The Quran explicitly forbids criticism.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' sacrifices and role as transmitters of Islam make reviling them a violation of Sunni principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you spoken negatively about a Companion or allowed others to do so without correction? How will you apply this principle from now on?
?
The Companions endured hardships to preserve the religion you follow. What is one sacrifice you can make today to honor their legacy?
?
If someone asks you about a controversial incident involving a Companion, how will you now respond with the lens this passage provides?

Evidence from Nabidh al-Jarr: Protecting Companions' Honor
Nasafi uses Abu Hanifa's ruling on nabidh al-jarr as evidence for protecting Companions from tafsiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Hanifa's ruling on nabidh al-jarr serves as a practical application of the principle of protecting the Companions' honor.

Core Idea
Declaring nabidh al-jarr prohibited would imply Companions sinned, so it must be avoided.

This lesson presents a concrete example from Abu Hanifa showing how theological principles translate into rulings. The author links the prohibition of reviling Companions directly to a legal principle regarding nabidh al-jarr, demonstrating the practical implications of protecting their honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument
Read the second part of the passage where Nasafi presents Abu Hanifa's condition regarding nabidh al-jarr.
2
Trace the logic
Follow the logical chain: Companions drank nabidh al-jarr; if it were prohibited, they would be sinners; but calling them sinners is a bid'ah; therefore, it cannot be prohibited.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider how this example illustrates the broader principle of refraining from reviling the Companions and how it shapes Islamic legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلموا أن من أصول مذهب السنة والجماعة كف اللسان عن الوقيعة في الصحابة، وحمل أمرهم على ما يوجب دفع الطعن والقدح عنهم؛ إذ هم الذين بذلوا أنفسهم وأموالهم، وودعوا الدعة والراحة، وتحملوا المشاق العظيمة في نصرة دين الله تعالى وهم نقلة الدين إلى من بعدهم وهم المكرمون بصحبة خير البشر ونصرته وإيوائه ووقايته بأنفسهم والجود بمهجهم دونه، ولهذا جعل أبو حنيفة من شرائط السنة أن لا يحرم نبيذ الجر لما أن في تحريمه تفسيق كبار الصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - لما ثبت بطريق لا شبهة فيه شربهم نبيذ الجر، ولو كان محرما لأوجب لك فسقهم، فكان القول بحرمته موجبا تفسيقهم، والقول بتفسيقهم بدعة وخروج عن شرائط مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة.
Then know that among the principles of the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a is restraining the tongue from reviling the Companions, and interpreting their affairs in a manner that necessitates repelling criticism and disparagement against them; for they are those who sacrificed themselves and their wealth, abandoned ease and comfort, and endured great hardships in supporting the religion of Allah Almighty, and they are the transmitters of the religion to those after them, and they are honored with the companionship of the best of mankind, and supporting him, giving him refuge, protecting him with their lives, and generously offering their souls for his sake. For this reason, Abu Hanifa made it among the conditions of the Sunna that one not declare nabidh al-jarr (date-wine) prohibited, because declaring it prohibited would entail declaring major Companions - may Allah be pleased with them - as sinners, since it is established by an unambiguous path that they drank nabidh al-jarr. Had it been prohibited, it would necessarily have necessitated their sinfulness. So the statement of its prohibition necessitates declaring them sinful, and declaring them sinful is an innovation and a departure from the conditions of the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage states a core principle of Ahl al-Sunna: refraining from reviling the Companions. The author gives two justifications: the Companions sacrificed everything for Islam and transmitted the religion, so they deserve honor. Then he provides a practical example from Abu Hanifa: making it a condition of the Sunna not to declare nabidh al-jarr prohibited, because doing so would necessitate declaring major Companions sinful since they drank it. Since declaring the Companions sinful is contrary to Ahl al-Sunna, the prohibition is rejected.

Key Terms
نبيذ الجر
التفسيق
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think nabidh al-jarr is inherently prohibited because it is an intoxicant.
Correction: The passage argues that even if it were intoxicating, the prohibition cannot be declared because it would necessitate accusing the Companions of sin, which is contrary to Sunni principles.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did Abu Hanifa make not prohibiting nabidh al-jarr a condition of the Sunna?
A) Because he believed it was actually permissible.
B) To avoid implying that the Companions who drank it were sinful.
C) Because it is clearly prohibited in the Quran.
D) To align with the practice of the Umayyads.

Key Takeaway
Protecting the Companions from accusations of sin can override even a potential legal prohibition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a religious ruling that would force you to assume the worst about a known righteous person, do you reconsider your position, or do you forge ahead without thought for their honor?
?
How often do you weigh the consequences of your theological stances on the reputation of the Companions and early Muslims? Could your current beliefs inadvertently disparage them?
?
If protecting the honor of the Companions overrides even a potential legal prohibition, what does that demand of you when you speak about their actions today?

Defending the Companions: Ijtihad and Excusable Differences
Nasafi responds to the objection that Companion conflicts justify reviling them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the disagreements and conflicts among the Companions do not justify reviling them, and how the principle of ijtihad and interpretation excuses their actions.

Core Idea
Disagreements among Companions were matters of ijtihad, not sinfulness.

This lesson addresses a critical objection against Sunni orthodoxy: if some Companions fought each other, doesn't that justify criticizing them? Al-Nasafi answers by explaining that their actions were based on ijtihad, and that even harsh words were for discipline. Understanding this defense is essential for maintaining respect for the entire generation of Companions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the objection carefully: the objectors claim that since some Companions shed each other's blood, they are sinful, and thus prohibiting reviling is itself a form of reviling, making the proponents Rafidis.
Notice the attempt to turn the argument back on the orthodox position.
2
Examine the core response
Nasafi begins by limiting the criticism to error in interpretation, not sinfulness, and cites 'Ali's words 'Our brethren have rebelled against us' to show that even the wronged party did not declare them sinful.
This sets the tone for the rest of the argument.
3
Learn the principle of ijtihad
The key principle: mujtahids who err are excused because they exerted their effort. Nasafi attributes this to Imam al-Maturidi and emphasizes that all disputes among Companions were of this kind.
This is the doctrinal foundation for excusing the Companions.
4
Analyze the purpose of fighting
The fighting was not for worldly gain but to resolve rancor and restore harmony. Nasafi implies that it was a necessary means to achieve unity.
Consider how this refutes the accusation of sinfulness.
5
Consider harsh speech and modern implications
Even harsh words like those of 'Umar to 'Ubada were for discipline ('ta'zir'), not condemnation. Today, reviling Companions amounts to belittling the transmitters of religion and reveals hidden animosity toward Islam itself.
Thus, reviling the Companions reflects poorly on the reviler's own faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: إنكم تزعمون أن الوقيعة في الصحابة غير جائزة، ومن طعن فيهم واشتغل بالوقيعة فيهم فهو طعن البعض على البعض بل قصد رافضي، والصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - البعض إراقة دم البعض فصار بعضهم فاسقا بذلك على زعمكم، فصرتم بمنعكم عن الطعن فيهم طاعنين فيهم وهو رفض عندكم فصرتم على زعمكم رافضة.
قلنا لهم ما ذكرتم من طعن البعض في البعض فلم يكن إلا قدر نسبتهم إلى الخطأ فيما ذهبوا إليه بتأويلهم، وما روي أن البعض منهم فسق البعض بل أكثر ما روي أن عليا قال فيهم : - إخواننا بغوا علينا - وكيف تفسقون وقد مر أنهم صاروا إلى ما صاروا مجتهدين، ثم الأصل في الاجتهاد أن كل أمر يحتمل العفو عنه والإباحة فيه، فمن أخطأ الحق في ذلك بالتأويل والاجتهاد فهو معذور، إذ بذل مجهوده وأنعم نظره فيما طمع أن يظفر فيه بالحق، وكذا ذكره الشيخ أبو منصور الماتريدي - رحمه الله - وكل خلاف كان بين الصحابة - رضي الله عنهم - كان من هذا القبيل إذ كان الله تعالى صان صحابة رسول الله عن اختلاف يوجب التضليل والتفسيق بفضله ورحمته، والقتال كان ليرتفع بالتباين ويعودوا إلى الألفة بعدما وقع بينهم من أسباب التضاغن عند انقطاع الطمع والرجاء عن العود إلى ذلك إلا بالقتال على ما قررنا والله المحمود. خشن القول قُصد به التعزير: ولو ثبت من البعض أنه واجه غيره بخشن من القول فذلك على وجه التعزير له على قلة تأمله فيما يجتهد كما قال عمر رضي الله عنه لعبادة في أمر المثلث: يا أحمق، وللإمام إقامة التعزير بما يرى من المصلحة به، فأما اليوم فلا معنى لبسط اللسان فيهم إلا التهاون بنقلة الدين وناصريه، وإظهار ما أضمر الطاعن عن الحقد عليهم بسبب إظهارهم الدين الحق وقيامهم بنصرته وسعيهم في تمحيق الكفر والباطل، وقطع دابر أهله، فصار بالطعن فيهم مطعونًا في دينه، وبالله العصمة.
If they say: You claim that reviling the Companions is impermissible. Whoever disparages them and occupies himself with reviling them is [in fact] reviling some of them against others, but rather it is a Rafidi intention, and the Companions - may Allah be pleased with them - some of them shed the blood of others, so some of them became sinful by that according to your claim. So by your prohibition of reviling them, you are reviling them, and that is Rafd (rejection) according to you, so you become, according to your claim, Rafidis.
We say to them: What you mentioned regarding the reviling of some of them against others was only to the extent of attributing error to them regarding what they pursued by way of their interpretation. And it is not reported that any of them declared another sinful. Rather the most that is reported is that 'Ali said about them: 'Our brethren have rebelled against us.' And how can you declare them sinful when it has been mentioned that they arrived at what they arrived at as mujtahids. Then the principle regarding ijtihad is that every matter is susceptible to being pardoned and permitted. So whoever errs regarding the truth in that due to interpretation and ijtihad is excused, for he exerted his effort and directed his contemplation towards what he hoped to attain of the truth. This is what Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi - may Allah have mercy on him - mentioned. And every dispute that occurred among the Companions - may Allah be pleased with them - was of this kind, for Allah Almighty preserved the Companions of His Messenger from a dispute that would necessitate misguidance or sinfulness by His bounty and mercy. And the fighting was so that through the divergence they would rise and return to harmony after there occurred between them causes of rancor when hope and expectation of returning to that was cut off except through fighting, as we have established. And Allah is Praiseworthy. Harsh speech was intended as discipline. And if it is established from some of them that he confronted another with harsh speech, that was for the purpose of disciplining him for his lack of reflection in his ijtihad, as 'Umar - may Allah be pleased with him - said to 'Ubada regarding the matter of the triangle: 'O foolish one!' And the Imam has the right to implement discipline as he sees of benefit. As for today, there is no meaning to spreading the tongue against them except belittling the transmitters of the religion and its supporters, and revealing what the reviler harbors of hatred against them due to their manifesting the true religion, their standing in supporting it, and their striving to obliterate disbelief and falsehood and cut off the root of its people. So by reviling them, one becomes reviled in his religion. And with Allah is protection.
Source pages p. 525

Commentary
This passage contains an objection and its answer. The objectors argue that since some Companions fought and shed blood, they are sinful, so reviling them is justified. They claim that the author's prohibition of reviling is itself a form of reviling, making them Rafidis. The author responds by stating that any criticism was only regarding errors in interpretation, not sinfulness. He cites 'Ali's statement calling them 'our brethren' to show they were not declared sinful. The author then explains the principle of ijtihad: mujtahids are excused for mistakes. The fighting was to resolve conflict and restore unity. Harsh words were for discipline, as shown by 'Umar's rebuke. Today, reviling them shows disdain for the transmitters of religion and reveals hatred. Thus, the reviler is actually reviling his own religion.

Key Terms
الوقيعة
الاجتهاد
التأويل
التعزير
الروافض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that disagreements and fighting among Companions indicate they were sinful and thus justify reviling them.
Correction: The passage explains that they were mujtahids whose errors in interpretation are excused, and the fighting was a means to restore harmony, not sinful.

Checkpoint
What is the main argument used by the author to defend the Companions who fought each other?
A) They were forced to fight.
B) They were mujtahids and mistakes in ijtihad are excused.
C) They repented afterwards.
D) Only some of them were sinful.

Key Takeaway
The disagreements among Companions were matters of legitimate ijtihad, and reviling them is a reflection on one's own faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about conflicts among the Companions, does your heart feel respect and awe, or does it entertain subtle criticism? What does that reaction reveal about your faith in Allah's choice of the Sahaba?
?
If you were in a disagreement with a fellow Muslim over a matter of interpretation, would you be quick to accuse them of sin, or would you pause and consider the principle of ijtihad that excuses them? How can you implement this principle in your daily interactions?
?
The passage says that reviling the Companions belittles the transmitters of the religion and harms one's own faith. Are there any Companions you have spoken lightly about, even in jest? What must you do to guard your tongue and heart from this?

Consensus on Abu Bakr's Superiority
Nasafi states the consensus on Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ahl al-Sunna holds a consensus that Abu Bakr is the best of the Companions after the Prophet, and how this contrasts with the Rawafid position.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna's consensus: Abu Bakr is the best of the Ummah after the Prophet.

This short but significant passage establishes a foundational doctrine of Sunni Islam: the consensus on Abu Bakr al-Siddiq's superiority among the Companions. Nasafi presents this as a settled matter, contrasting it with the opposing view of the Rawafid. Understanding this consensus helps clarify a key point of Sunni theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Notice how brief and definitive the language is.
Nasafi uses the term 'Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a' to signal orthodoxy.
2
Identify the consensus and the two groups
Identify that the passage states a consensus (ijma') on Abu Bakr being the best, and then mentions the Rawafid as holding a different view. Note the contrast.
'Rawafid' is a term for Shia who reject the first three caliphs.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'afdal'
Consider what 'best' (afdal) means here: it is about excellence and rank, not personal preference. The passage asserts this as a matter of religious knowledge.
This relates to the Sunni doctrine of the virtues of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في أن أبا بكر أفضل الصحابة
أجمع أهل السنة والجماعة على أن أفضل هذه الأمة بعد نبيها أبو بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه، فأما الروافض بأجمعهم فإنهم يزعمون أن أفضل الأمة علي رضي الله عنه.
Discussion on the fact that Abu Bakr is the best of the Companions. Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a are in consensus that the best of this Ummah after its Prophet is Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. As for the Rawafid collectively, they claim that the best of the Ummah is 'Ali, may Allah be pleased with him.
Source pages p. 526

Commentary
This passage briefly states a key doctrine of Ahl al-Sunna: the consensus (ijma') that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq is the most excellent of the Companions after the Prophet. It contrasts this with the position of the Rawafid (a term for the Shia who reject the first three caliphs), who claim that 'Ali is the best. The passage thus establishes a clear line of orthodoxy.

Key Terms
أفضل
أبو بكر الصديق
الروافض
علي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That superiority is based on personal opinion or family relationship.
Correction: The passage shows it is a matter of scholarly consensus (ijma') of Ahl al-Sunna, not personal preference.

Checkpoint

A) Abu Bakr
B) Umar
C) Uthman
D) Ali

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna agrees that Abu Bakr al-Siddiq is the most excellent of the Companions after the Prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Is your heart fully at peace with this consensus, or do you harbor any doubt from whispers that elevate personal preference over the collective judgment of the Ummah? What would you say to yourself if you felt a pull toward the view of the Rawafid?
?
The Rawafid are described as 'collectively claiming' Ali's superiority. Have you ever felt drawn to elevate a figure above the rank established by the consensus of the Salaf? Examine your feelings toward the Companions: is there any hidden partiality that contradicts the Sunni position taught here?
?
This lesson presents a consensus as a definitive truth. In what area of your life are you tempted to follow a minority opinion that goes against the clear consensus of the scholars? Will you submit to the truth even when it challenges your inclinations?

Sectarian Views on the Caliphate and Preference of Companions
Summarizes views of Imamiyya, Jarudiyya, Jaririyya, Ya'qubiyya, and Mu'tazila on caliphate and preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the diverse views of various Islamic sects on the caliphate and the relative merit of the Companions, including the positions of Imamiyya, Zaydi branches, and Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Different sects held sharply contrasting views on the caliphate and the ranking of Companions.

This passage from al-Nasafi's Tabsirat al-Adilla provides a concise survey of the main sectarian positions on the caliphate and the preference of Companions. It shows how the Imamiyya, various Zaydi groups, and the Mu'tazila differed on issues such as apostasy of Companions, legitimacy of the first two caliphs, and the superiority of Ali. Understanding these differences is key to grasping the theological landscape of early Islam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sects
Read the Arabic passage and translation, listing all sects mentioned: Imamiyya, Jarudiyya, Jaririyya, Ya'qubiyya, and Mu'tazila.
Notice that the Zaydi groups are further divided.
2
Imamiyya and Jarudiyya extremes
Note that the Imamiyya claim most Companions apostatized except Ali, his sons, Fatima, and a few. The Jarudiyya declare Abu Bakr a disbeliever.
Both hold extreme views against the early caliphs.
3
Jaririyya and Ya'qubiyya moderation
The Jaririyya affirm Abu Bakr and Umar's imamate and condemn the Jarudiyya. The Ya'qubiyya also show loyalty but do not disavow those who disavow them. Both still prefer Ali over all Companions.
This shows a spectrum within Zaydiyya.
4
Mu'tazila positions
Most later Mu'tazila follow the Jaririyya/Ya'qubiyya view of preferring Ali while affirming the first two caliphs. Al-Ka'bi explicitly chose this. Al-Jubba'i suspended judgment, conditional on the bird hadith.
This shows diversity even within Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الإمامية فأكثرهم على أن من سوى علي وابنيه وفاطمة ونفر يسير من الصحابة ارتدوا بعد وفاة النبي عليه السلام، وكذا الجارودية من الزيدية يكفرون أبا بكر [؟] الله، فأما الجريرية من الزيدية وهم أصحاب سليمان بن جرير رؤساء الزيدية، فإنهم يثبتون إمامة أبي بكر وعمر رضي الله عنهما ويكفرون الجارودية منهم في إكفارهم أبا بكر وعمر وكذا اليعقوبية من الزيدية يتولون أبا بكر وعمر غير أنهم لا يتبرون [؟] ممن يتبرأ من أبي بكر وعمر غير أن الجريرية واليعقوبية مع هذا يفضلون عليًا على جميع الصحابة، وإلى هذا يذهب أكثر متأخري المعتزلة، ونص الكعبي على اختياره هذا المذهب في كتابه المسمى بعيون المسائل، وأما الجبائي من جملة رؤساء المعتزلة فإنه كان يتوقف في ذلك وكان يقول : إن صح خبر الطير فعلي أفضل.
As for the Imamiyya, most of them hold that other than Ali, his two sons, Fatima, and a few companions apostatized after the death of the Prophet, peace be upon him. Likewise, the Jarudiyya of the Zaydiyya declare Abu Bakr [رضي الله عنه?] a disbeliever. As for the Jaririyya of the Zaydiyya, who are the followers of Sulayman ibn Jarir, the leaders of the Zaydiyya, they affirm the imamate of Abu Bakr and Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, and declare the Jarudiyya among them disbelievers for their declaration of disbelief in Abu Bakr and Umar. Likewise, the Ya'qubiyya of the Zaydiyya show loyalty to Abu Bakr and Umar, but they do not disavow [؟] those who disavow Abu Bakr and Umar. However, the Jaririyya and Ya'qubiyya, despite this, prefer Ali over all the companions. To this goes the majority of the later Mu'tazila, and al-Ka'bi explicitly stated his choice of this doctrine in his book titled 'Uyun al-Masa'il. As for al-Jubba'i, among the leading Mu'tazila, he hesitated on this and used to say: If the hadith of the bird is authentic, then Ali is the best.
Source pages p. 527

Commentary
This passage classifies the views of several sects regarding the caliphate and the relative merit of the companions. The author begins with the Imamiyya (Twelver Shia), who hold that most companions apostatized after the Prophet's death, except Ali, his sons, Fatima, and a few others. Next, the Jarudiyya, a branch of the Zaydiyya, are described as declaring Abu Bakr a disbeliever. The Jaririyya, another Zaydi branch, affirm the imamate of Abu Bakr and Umar, and in turn declare the Jarudiyya disbelievers for their extreme position. The Ya'qubiyya, also Zaydi, show loyalty to Abu Bakr and Umar but do not disavow those who disavow them. Yet, both the Jaririyya and Ya'qubiyya consider Ali superior to all other companions. The author then notes that this view—preferring Ali while affirming the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar—is adopted by most later Mu'tazila, and al-Ka'bi explicitly chose it in his work. Finally, al-Jubba'i, another leading Mu'tazilite, suspended judgment, saying that if the hadith of the bird (which indicates Ali's merit) is authentic, then Ali is the best.

Key Terms
الإمامية
الجارودية
الجريرية
اليعقوبية
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Zaydi groups hold the same view on the caliphate.
Correction: The passage shows significant variation: Jarudiyya are extreme, Jaririyya moderate, Ya'qubiyya nuanced.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Zaydi group declares Abu Bakr and Umar disbelievers?
A) Al-Jabba'i
B) Al-Jaririyya
C) Al-Jarudiyya
D) Al-Ya'qubiyya

Key Takeaway
The early Islamic sects displayed a wide range of views on the caliphate and the ranking of Companions, from extreme condemnation to qualified preference.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jaririyya and Ya'qubiyya managed to hold loyalty to Abu Bakr and Umar while still preferring Ali. Where do you stand in your own heart? Are you able to honor all of the Prophet's companions without needing to rank them, or do you find yourself drawn to a hierarchy? What does that reveal about your attachment to the early Muslim community?
?
Al-Jubba'i hesitated to declare Ali the best because he was uncertain about the authenticity of the hadith of the bird. How much of your own religious beliefs have you personally examined versus simply inherited? Is there a teaching you hold that might be conditional on a proof you have not verified?
?
The Imamiyya claim that most Companions apostatized after the Prophet's death. When you hear a fellow Muslim speak negatively about a Companion today, what is your immediate reaction? Does it anger you, sadden you, or does it leave you indifferent? What does your reaction say about your understanding of the Prophet's legacy?

Abu Bakr's Steadfastness at the Prophet's Passing
Al-Nasafi enumerates Abu Bakr's decisive actions after the Prophet's death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Bakr's firmness and decisive actions at the death of the Prophet and during the apostasy demonstrate his superior intellect and leadership.

Core Idea
Abu Bakr's unshaken faith guided the community through its greatest crisis.

This passage highlights Abu Bakr's unique composure when the death of the Prophet plunged the Companions into confusion. While some denied the death and others claimed the Prophet still lived, Abu Bakr remained steadfast, reciting the Quranic verse confirming mortality. His subsequent decisions—dispatching Usama's army and fighting the apostates—restored stability. This lesson examines these proofs of his superiority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the opening phrase describing Abu Bakr's qualities—these set the stage.
2
Identify the three challenges
The passage presents three specific challenges Abu Bakr faced: the Prophet's death, the dispatch of Usama's army, and the fight against apostates. Find each one and note how Abu Bakr responded.
Each response flows from his firmness and intellect.
3
Reflect on the qualities
Think about how Abu Bakr's actions exemplify the qualities listed at the beginning: strength of intellect, correctness of planning, firmness of composure, and bravery. How do these manifest in each situation?
This connects the explicit description to the narrative proof.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
على قوة عقله، وإصابة تدبيره، ورباطة جأشه، وغاية شجاعته، وقلة مبالاته بلومة اللائمين، فإن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم - كانوا لما حزبهم الأمر العظيم والخطب الهائل الجليل بوفاة رسول الله تحيروا في ذلك، حتى كان منهم من أنكر موته كراهة شق عصا المسلمين وتفرق كلمتهم، ومنهم من ادعى حياته عليه السلام لما ظن أنه لا يموت إذ هو خاتم الأنبياء، فهو عند ذلك ثبت قلبه ولم يتحير في أمره، وما ذهل عن رأيه عند نزول الخطب الذي لمثله يكترث ولدى حلوله إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ ثم أنفذ جيش أسامة على خوف المسلمين التفرق والانقلاب وقال: لا أحل لواء عقده رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم إنه فعل ما فعل بأهل الردة وبمانعي الزكاة فهدى الله تعالى ببركة سعيه العرب بعدما نكصوا عن الدين على أعقابهم وارتدوا على أدبارهم، والله الموفق. وكذا تفويض النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أمر الصلاة إليه مع قوله عليه السلام: يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله تعالى الحديث، دل أنه كان أفضلهم، ولهذا قال له علي لما قال: أقيلوني - فقام علي فقال: لا نقيلك ولا نستقيلك قدمك رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا نؤخرك رضيك لديننا فرضيناك لدنيانا وكذا لما قال أبو سفيان لعلي حين بويع أبو بكر: ما بال هذا الأمر في أذل قبيلة من قريش، لو شئت ملأتها عليهم خيلاً ورجالاً - قال له علي: طال ما عاديت الإسلام وأهله أنا وجدتها أبا بكر لها أهلاً - فهذه الدلائل تدل على كونه أفضل الصحابة، والله الموفق.
Upon the strength of his intellect, correctness of his planning, firmness of his composure, utmost bravery, and lack of concern for the blame of blamers. For the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, when the great matter and tremendous, grave calamity of the death of the Messenger of Allah befell them, they were confused about it, to the point that some of them denied his death out of dislike of splitting the staff of the Muslims and dispersing their word, and some of them claimed his life, peace be upon him, because they thought he would not die since he is the seal of the prophets. But he (Abu Bakr) at that time his heart was firm and he was not confused about his affair, nor was he distracted from his opinion when the calamity descended, which for its like one is distressed and upon its occurrence (the verse) 'Indeed you are mortal and indeed they are mortal' (39:30). Then he dispatched the army of Usama despite the Muslims' fear of division and reversal, and said: 'I will not untie a banner that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, tied.' Then he did what he did with the people of apostasy and the preventers of Zakat, so Allah guided the Arabs by the blessing of his effort after they had recoiled from the religion on their heels and apostatized on their backs. And Allah is the granter of success. Likewise, the delegation of the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, of the matter of prayer to him with his statement, peace be upon him: 'The most reciter among you of the Book of Allah leads you in prayer' – the hadith – indicated that he was the most excellent of them. For this reason, Ali said to him when he said: 'Discharge me,' so Ali stood and said: 'We will not discharge you nor seek your discharge; the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, put you forward, we will not put you back. He approved you for our religion, so we approve you for our worldly lives.' Likewise, when Abu Sufyan said to Ali when Abu Bakr was given allegiance: 'What is this matter in the most despised tribe of Quraysh? If you wish, I will fill it against them with horses and men.' Ali said to him: 'You have long been hostile to Islam and its people. I found Abu Bakr worthy of it.' So these proofs indicate that he was the most excellent of the Companions. And Allah is the granter of success.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is the concluding part of an argument for Abu Bakr's superiority over the other Companions. The author, al-Nasafi, first recounts Abu Bakr's steadfastness at the Prophet's death: while many Companions were confused and either denied the death or claimed the Prophet was still alive, Abu Bakr remained firm. He then cites Abu Bakr's decisive actions: sending Usama's army despite fear of division, and fighting the apostates and those who refused Zakat, which restored the Arabs to Islam after apostasy. Next, the author mentions the Prophet's delegation of leading prayer to Abu Bakr, based on the hadith 'the most reciter among you leads you,' implying Abu Bakr was the best. Ali's own statement supporting Abu Bakr's caliphate is quoted, as well as Ali's rejection of Abu Sufyan's offer to oppose Abu Bakr. The author concludes that these proofs demonstrate Abu Bakr's excellence over all other Companions.

Key Terms
الردة
مانعي الزكاة
رباطة جأش

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Abu Bakr's actions after the Prophet's death were purely political and not based on religious conviction.
Correction: The passage shows his actions were grounded in faith and obedience to the Prophet. He recited a Quranic verse, followed the Prophet's orders, and fought to preserve the religion, not for power.

Checkpoint
What verse did Abu Bakr recite at the Prophet's death?
A) إِنَّكَ مَيِّتٌ وَإِنَّهُم مَّيِّتُونَ
B) يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا اتَّقُوا اللَّهَ
C) قُلْ هُوَ اللَّهُ أَحَدٌ
D) وَلَقَدْ نَصَرَكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي مَوَاطِنَ كَثِيرَةٍ

Key Takeaway
Abu Bakr's unwavering faith and resolute leadership at the Prophet's death and during the apostasy prove his superiority among the Companions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When a great trial shakes your faith, do you remain firm like Abu Bakr or do you waver like some Companions? What verse or action will you cling to when your certainty is tested?
?
Abu Bakr disregarded the blame of blamers. Whose opinion do you fear more than Allah's? Are you willing to stand alone for the truth?
?
The Prophet's death was the greatest crisis. What is the greatest trial you have faced, and how did your faith guide you? If you were to face it again, what would you do differently based on this lesson?

Prophetic Delegation and Ali's Endorsement of Abu Bakr
Al-Nasafi presents the Prophet's appointment of Abu Bakr as prayer leader and Ali's support as proofs of Abu Bakr's superiority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's delegation of prayer to Abu Bakr and the support of Ali demonstrate Abu Bakr's excellence over the Companions.

Core Idea
The Prophet's choice and Ali's words confirm Abu Bakr's unmatched virtue.

This passage continues the proofs for Abu Bakr's superiority by citing the Prophet's decision to appoint him as imam in prayer, which according to the hadith indicates the most excellent. Additionally, Ali's words rejecting Abu Bakr's resignation and his response to Abu Sufyan's offer further solidify Abu Bakr's status. This lesson explores these testimonies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice the transition from the previous section with 'وكذا' (likewise).
This part introduces two new proofs: the prayer delegation and Ali's statements.
2
Understand the significance of the prayer delegation
The Prophet put Abu Bakr forward to lead prayer, and the hadith 'يؤمكم أقرؤكم لكتاب الله' implies that the best reciter leads. The author argues this shows Abu Bakr was the most excellent.
Think about why leading prayer is a sign of virtue.
3
Analyze Ali's statements
Ali said two things: first, when Abu Bakr offered to resign, Ali insisted he was placed by the Prophet; second, when Abu Sufyan proposed to overthrow Abu Bakr, Ali rejected it and declared Abu Bakr worthy. Consider how these statements support Abu Bakr's superiority.
Note that Ali's authority as a key Companion adds weight to his testimony.

A) 'We will not discharge you nor seek your discharge'

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How does the Prophet's choice of Abu Bakr to lead prayer challenge your own tendency to judge others by worldly status? Is there someone God has placed in authority over you—a parent, teacher, or leader—whom you struggle to respect because of their background? What would change if you saw them as divinely appointed?
?
Ali publicly defended Abu Bakr despite potential tribal pressure and personal cost. Is there a person in your community whom God has clearly blessed or elevated, yet you privately resent due to jealousy or pride? What would it require for you to openly affirm them as Ali did?
?
The hadith 'يؤمكم أقرؤكم' ties leadership to Quranic knowledge. Are you actively striving to increase your connection with the Book of Allah so that you might be worthy of leading others, even in your own home? What specific step will you take this week to deepen your engagement with the Quran?

Rafidi Claims and Refutation of the Bird Hadith
Objection-and-answer: Rafidi proofs and refutation of the bird hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main Rafidi arguments for Ali's superiority and how the author refutes the key proof (the hadith of the bird) by declaring it fabricated and citing a more authentic and contrary tradition.

Core Idea
The Rafidi case relies on a fabricated hadith; authentic narrations show others as most beloved.

In this passage, the author presents several arguments the Rawafid (extreme Shi'a) use to prove Ali's superiority over the other Companions, including claims based on specific hadiths, knowledge, courage, and purity from shirk. He then focuses on refuting the most prominent proof—the hadith of the bird—by exposing it as fabricated and offering a more famous, authentic hadith that contradicts it. This lesson unpacks both the claims and the refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Rafidi arguments
Read the first part of the passage where the author lists the proofs: the bird hadith, brotherhood, city of knowledge, most judging, courage, jihad, and never committing shirk.
Notice these are claims the author attributes to the Rawafid, not his own views.
2
Identify the refutation's target
The author chooses to refute only the hadith of the bird. He declares it fabricated (منحولة) and provides a sound chain for a different wording.
The wording difference changes the meaning: 'most beloved to me' vs. 'most beloved to You'.
3
Understand the counter-hadith
The author then cites a more famous hadith where the Prophet names Aisha and Abu Bakr (as 'Abu Hashim') as the most beloved people, directly challenging the Rafidi inference.
This shows that even if the bird hadith were authentic, it would be overridden by stronger evidence.
4
Reflect on the method
Consider how the author uses hadith criticism (declaring fabrication) and mutual contradiction (ta'arud) to refute a sectarian argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أدلة الروافض على أفضلية علي والرد عليهم ثم عهدة ما تعلق الروافض به من تفضيل علي على غيره من الصحابة ما روى أن النبي عليه السلام قال : اللهم ائتني بأحب خلقك إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطير فجاءه علي، فدل أنه أحب خلق الله إليه وأحبهم إليه أفضلهم، وكذا يحتجون بالمروي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أخوه، وكذا يقولون: إنه كان أعلم الصحابة بدليل قوله عليه السلام أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها وبدليل قوله عليه السلام: أقضاكم علي وكونه أشجع الناس لا ريب فيه، وكذا يتعلقون بكثرة جهاده وقتله أعداء الله تعالى ولم يدانه في ذلك أحد من الصحابة، وكذا يقولون: إنه لم يشرك بالله طرفة عين بخلاف غيره. والجواب عن تعلقهم بخبر الطير أن هذه الرواية منحولة، والصحيح من الروايات أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قال: ائتني بأحب خلقك إلي هكذا حدثنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن نصر الجميلي بإسناد صحيح، ثم هو معارض بما هو أشهر منه روى عن النبي أنه لو قيل له: من أحب الناس إليك قال: عائشة قيل من الرجال، قال أبو هاشم هو ما دل معناه بأحب خلقك إلى عند النقلة وهو ما
Proofs of the Rawafid regarding the superiority of Ali and the refutation of them. Then the citation of what the Rawafid cling to regarding preferring Ali over the rest of the Companions: what is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'O Allah, bring me the most beloved of Your creation to You to eat with me from this bird,' so Ali came to him, so it indicated that he was the most beloved of Allah's creation to Him, and the most beloved of them to Him is the most excellent of them. Likewise they argue with the narrated that he, peace and blessings be upon him, is his brother. And likewise they say: he was the most knowledgeable of the Companions, based on his statement, peace be upon him: 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' and based on his statement, peace be upon him: 'The most judging among you is Ali.' And that he was the most courageous of people – no doubt about it. And likewise they cling to the abundance of his jihad and his killing of the enemies of Allah, and no one of the Companions rivaled him in that. And likewise they say: he never associated anything with Allah even for the twinkle of an eye, unlike others. And the answer regarding their clinging to the hadith of the bird is that this narration is fabricated. The correct narration is that he, peace be upon him, said: 'Bring me the most beloved of Your creation to me' – thus narrated to us the Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Jumayli with a sound chain. Then it is opposed by that which is more famous than it: it is narrated from the Prophet that if it were said to him: 'Who is the most beloved of people to you?' he said: 'Aisha.' It was said: 'Among men?' He said: 'Abu Hashim' – and its meaning indicates 'the most beloved of creation to you' according to the transmitters, and it is what...
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. The author first presents the Rafidi (Shi'a) arguments for Ali's superiority over the other Companions. These include: the hadith of the bird (where Ali was called the most beloved), the hadith of brotherhood, the hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate', the hadith 'the most judging among you is Ali', Ali's unmatched courage and jihad, and the claim that he never committed shirk. The author then provides a refutation focusing on the hadith of the bird, declaring it fabricated (منحولة) and citing a more authentic version where the wording is 'bring me the most beloved of creation to me' (not 'to You'). Furthermore, the author mentions a more famous hadith where the Prophet said the most beloved people to him were Aisha (among women) and Abu Bakr (among men, referred to as 'Abu Hashim' – a variant name for Abu Bakr). This counteracts the Rafidi claim. The passage ends abruptly while discussing the meaning of the alternative version.

Key Terms
الروافض
خبر الطير
منحولة
الأحب
أبو هاشم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith of the bird (with wording 'to You') is authentic and proves Ali is the most beloved to Allah.
Correction: The author shows it is fabricated (منحولة) and that the authentic wording is 'to me', and even then it is contradicted by a more famous hadith where the Prophet names Aisha and Abu Bakr as most beloved.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the Rafidi argument based on the hadith of the bird?
A) He accepts the hadith but reinterprets its meaning
B) He denies that Ali came to the Prophet on that occasion
C) He declares the narration fabricated and cites a more authentic version
D) He argues the bird was not a real event

Key Takeaway
The Rafidi claim based on the bird hadith is invalid because the narration is fabricated and authentic traditions place others as more beloved.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Rafidi arguments, do you feel any emotional pull towards Ali's virtues? How does learning that a key proof is fabricated challenge your trust in narratives that align with your biases? Will you commit to verifying the authenticity of every hadith you base your beliefs on?
?
The refutation shows that the most beloved people to the Prophet were Aisha and Abu Bakr. Do you harbor any hidden dislike or prejudice against these Companions in your heart? What concrete step can you take today to purify your love for them in accordance with the Prophet's example?

The Rawafid's Arguments for Ali's Superiority
Lists the Rawafid's proofs for preferring Ali over other companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seven arguments the Rawafid use to claim Ali's superiority over other companions.

Core Idea
The Rawafid's case for Ali's superiority rests on several hadiths and personal merits.

In this passage, Imam al-Nasafi presents the arguments of the Rawafid (a sect later known as Shia) for preferring Ali over all other companions. These arguments are based on specific hadiths, Ali's bravery, jihad, and his unique status of never having committed shirk. Understanding these claims is essential before the author refutes them in subsequent lessons.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Get an overview of the arguments.
Notice the phrase 'ثم عهدة' indicates the author is now listing what the Rawafid cling to.
2
Identify each distinct argument
The passage lists seven arguments. Find each one and note the evidence cited (hadith, bravery, etc.).
The arguments are: bird hadith, brotherhood hadith, city of knowledge hadith, best judge hadith, bravery, jihad, never committing shirk.
3
Analyze the rhetorical structure
Ask yourself: why does the author list these arguments without any refutation here? This sets up later critique.
This passage is a summary of the opponent's position, which will be answered.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
One might think these are irrefutable proofs, but the author will later show their weaknesses. Be critical.
Consider how each argument might be challenged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم عهدة ما تعلق الروافض به من تفضيل علي على غيره من الصحابة ما روى أن النبي عليه السلام قال: "اللهم ائتني بأحب خلقك إليك يأكل معي من هذا الطير" فجاءه علي له، فدل أنه أحب خلق الله إليه وأحبهم إليه أفضلهم، وكذا يحتجون بالمروي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أخوه، وكذا يقولون: إنه كان أعلم الصحابة بدليل قوله عليه السلام: "أنا مدينة العلم وعلى بابها" وبدليل قوله عليه السلام: "أقضاكم علي" وكونه أشجع الناس لا ريب فيه، وكذا يتعلقون بكثرة جهاده وقتله أعداء الله تعالى ولم يدانه في ذلك أحد من الصحابة، وكذا يقولون: إنه لم يشرك بالله طرفة عين بخلاف غيره.
Then, what the Rawafid have clung to in preferring Ali over other companions includes that it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O Allah, bring me the most beloved of Your creation to You to eat with me from this bird,' so Ali came to him, and it indicates that he is the most beloved of Allah's creation to Him, and the most beloved to Him is the most virtuous. And similarly they argue by the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) is his brother. And they say: He was the most knowledgeable of the companions by the evidence of his saying (peace be upon him): 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' and by his saying: 'The best judge among you is Ali.' And that he was the bravest of people, no doubt about it. And they cling to his abundant jihad and killing of Allah's enemies, and no one among the companions equaled him in that. And they say: He never associated anything with Allah for the blink of an eye, unlike others.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage enumerates the arguments used by the Rawafid (a sect that later became known as Shia) to prove that Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) is superior to all other companions. The author presents these arguments without yet refuting them, as a record of their claims. The arguments include: 1) The hadith of the bird, where the Prophet asked Allah to bring the most beloved person to eat with him, and Ali came, implying Ali is the most beloved to Allah and thus the most virtuous. 2) The hadith declaring the Prophet and Ali as brothers. 3) The hadith 'I am the city of knowledge and Ali is its gate,' suggesting Ali possesses exclusive knowledge. 4) The hadith 'The best judge among you is Ali,' indicating his superior judgment. 5) Ali's unmatched bravery. 6) His extensive jihad and killing of enemies. 7) That he never committed shirk even for a moment, unlike other companions (implying they had pre-Islamic polytheism). Each argument is presented without comment, allowing the reader to see the basis of the Rawafid position.

Key Terms
الروافض
تفضيل
خبر الطير
أنا مدينة العلم
أقضاكم علي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think these arguments are irrefutable proofs of Ali's absolute superiority over all companions.
Correction: These arguments are presented as the Rawafid's claims; the author will later show their weaknesses and provide counterarguments. They are not accepted as definitive by Sunni scholars.

Checkpoint
How many distinct arguments do the Rawafid use in this passage to claim Ali's superiority?
A) Three
B) Five
C) Seven
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
The Rawafid's arguments for Ali's superiority are a set of textual and ethical claims that need to be examined critically.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage shows that the Rawafid believe Ali never committed shirk even for a blink. But you and I live in a time where shirk may take subtle forms like seeking fame or showing off. When was the last time you caught yourself doing an act of worship for other than Allah? What will you do today to purify your intention?
?
The Rawafid use the hadith of the bird to argue that Ali is the most beloved to Allah. How does knowing that Allah loves those who obey Him affect the way you prioritize your daily actions? Are you living as someone who truly seeks to be among the most beloved?
?
If you had to defend the honor of all the Prophet's companions against these claims, what would you say to someone who argues that Ali's exclusive virtues make him superior? Does your answer rely on what you learned in this lesson, or on emotions? How can you prepare yourself to respond with knowledge rather than bias?
